## 2026-07-19

### Infrastructure
- **RCA-tiered Bash retry guard: differentiate signatures by stdout content, not stderr — closes a fleet-wide false-positive hard-block** - PR #6257 (SD-LEO-INFRA-RCA-TIERED-SIGNATURE-FALSE-POSITIVE-001)
  - **What shipped**: coordinator-confirmed RCA (session 89b12649, 169-session empirical proof): Claude Code's Bash `tool_response` never populates real `stderr` content or a numeric `exit_code` — a genuine failure's error text (confirmed even including an uncaught native crash) lands entirely in `stdout`, with zero distinguishing field between a success and a hard failure. The RCA-tiered 3x-Bash retry guard (`scripts/hooks/retry-state-manager.cjs`'s `signatureFor()`, fed by `scripts/hooks/post-tool-rca-outcome.cjs`) differentiated repeat-command signatures using ONLY `{exit_code, stderr_sha}` — both near-constant on this harness — so 3 legitimately-different failures of the same command collapsed into ONE signature and the 3-strikes rule could hard-block a correct 4th attempt (a real incident: `SD_TYPE_CHANGE_EXPLANATION_REQUIRED` → an anti-gaming threshold → `SD_TYPE_CHANGE_TIMING_BLOCKED` collapsed and blocked a now-correct retry). Fix: a new `digestStdoutTail()` (generalized from the existing `digestStderr`/`digestContent` bounded-window+normalization approach) captures `tool_response.stdout` and writes a `stdout_sha` field, which `signatureFor()` now mixes into the Bash outcome digest alongside the existing fields — additive only, the Control 1+2 read-only-command exemption and the separate progress-stall/auto-signal mechanisms are untouched. A new de-masking test (`tests/unit/rca-tiered-signature-real-payload.test.js`) uses ONLY the empirically-real payload shape, first proving the pre-fix collapse explicitly before proving the fix.
  - **LEAD-TO-PLAN VALIDATION caught a deeper, separate defect during adversarial review and it was handled honestly, not silently absorbed**: when a matching `command_sha` is carried on the prior outcome (the dominant real-world same-command-repeat shape), the pre-existing succeeding-poll exemption in `recordAndCount()` pre-empts this fix's signature differentiation entirely, since a different already-shipped feature (Control 4) infers `exit_code:0` from mere absence of a failure signal — for genuine failures too, not just successes. Rather than bundling a fix to that separately-shipped, separately-tested mechanism into this PR, it was filed as a first-class follow-up (`SD-LEO-INFRA-SUCCEEDING-POLL-EXEMPTION-001`, priority=high) with an honest `KNOWN LIMITATION` test documenting the current gap as a regression canary. That follow-up was independently claimed and completed by another fleet worker *during this SD's own build* — a genuine concurrent-fleet collision, resolved via a real `git merge` conflict combining both fixes (main's removal of the `exit_code:0` fabrication + this SD's `stdout_sha` capture, which turned out to be complementary: without `stdout_sha`, removing the fabrication would have made outcome capture write almost nothing at all for real Bash calls).
  - **Verification**: 162 tests pass repo-wide across every file referencing either hook (zero regressions), including 2 tests in the other worker's newly-merged e2e suite updated to reflect the correct combined behavior (a last-outcome file is now written for real content, but `exit_code` still correctly stays `null` so the exemption cannot misfire on it). Independent Explore + VALIDATION + TESTING (×2) + SECURITY sub-agent review, all PASS. SECURITY flagged one non-blocking hardening note (cap per-line length before hashing, since `stdout` is now hashed far more often than `stderr` ever was) — applied same-session. `/heal` scored 99/100. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 95, PLAN-TO-EXEC 93, EXEC-TO-PLAN 95, PLAN-TO-LEAD 97, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 99.
- **Adam decision-scheduler: wires the previously-unwired away-bridge to real production seams** - PR #6252 (SD-LEO-INFRA-ADAM-DECISION-SCHEDULER-001)
  - **What shipped**: the away-bridge (`lib/comms/adam-outbound/away-bridge/index.js`, a presence-gated re-surfacer for owed-but-unanswered chairman decisions shipped by a prior SD) had zero real caller — armed logic, no dispatcher. `lib/comms/adam-outbound/decision-scheduler/index.js` wires it to real seams: an `owedStore` adapter over `sms_outbound_obligations` (fail-soft while that STAGED migration remains unapplied — returns `[]`, never throws), a presence signal derived from `claude_sessions.heartbeat_at`, a `sender` wrapping the already-live chairman-sms-gate, and an `escalateEmail` wrapping the existing chairman decision-email path. `scripts/cron/adam-decision-scheduler-tick.mjs` is the durable `--once` cron runner (mirrors `chairman-decision-sla-sweep.mjs`'s shape), registers ARMED machinery (`periodic_process_registry`) with a pinned activation-trigger literal naming the STAGED-migration-apply event, and inlines a newly-authored, authoritative runtime DST-aware quiet-window guard (22:00-06:00 America/New_York — a different window from the existing 23:00-05:00 chairman/email quiet window, since no shared helper for this exact boundary existed repo-wide). A new `.github/workflows/adam-decision-scheduler-cron.yml` plus a `package.json` cron-script entry give both new files a real `WIRE_CHECK_GATE` reachability root. The stale `@wire-check-exempt` marker on `away-bridge/index.js` was removed now that it has a genuine caller (hygiene only — `WIRE_CHECK` only re-checks newly-added files, never modified ones).
  - **Two review rounds caught real PRD inaccuracies before/during EXEC, both fixed by amending the PRD directly**: LEAD-TO-PLAN VALIDATION corrected an assumption that removing the wire-check-exempt marker would make `WIRE_CHECK` re-evaluate `away-bridge/index.js` — it doesn't (modified files aren't re-checked); the real reachability gap was the two genuinely-new files, closed via the `package.json` entry point instead. PLAN-TO-EXEC TESTING corrected an inaccurate "zero-code activation" claim — the STAGED `sms_outbound_obligations` schema has no `answered`/`resurfaceCount`/`resurfacedThisWindow` columns, so real-column mapping needed explicit scoping (owedId←id, message←{body}, decision-only filter) with the unbacked fields' derivation/bookkeeping explicitly deferred to a documented chairman-apply follow-up rather than silently assumed free.
  - **Verification**: 25 new tests across 2 files (TS-1 table-absent fail-soft, TS-8 real-column mapping pinned against the STAGED schema — not just a friendly mock, TS-2 full tick-wiring through the real unmodified `processOwedDecisions` policy, TS-5/TS-6/TS-7/TS-9 static + behavioral wiring pins, TS-10 DST-aware quiet-window boundary math across EST/EDT and spring/fall transition dates), zero regressions across 68 tests in the surrounding comms suite. EXEC-TO-PLAN TESTING and SECURITY both independently re-verified (TESTING ran the cron live against the current table-absent DB and confirmed the true no-op path; SECURITY confirmed no new secrets, minimal GHA permissions, parameterized queries only, and that the sender/escalateEmail wrappers never bypass the existing gate's fail-closed rubric). `/heal` scored 98/100. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 95, PLAN-TO-EXEC 97, EXEC-TO-PLAN 94, PLAN-TO-LEAD 97, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 99.

## 2026-07-18

### Infrastructure
- **Archive 2 pre-guard duplicate EVA Intake Roadmap rows — LEO Roadmap confirmed as sole plan-of-record** - PR #6242 (SD-LEO-INFRA-ROADMAP-DUPLICATE-CLEANUP-001)
  - **What shipped**: chairman-confirmed 2026-07-17 that the LEO Roadmap (`strategic_roadmaps` id `3aa2f3e2`, active, vision-linked to `VISION-EHG-L1-001`) is the sole plan-of-record; EVA Intake Roadmaps retire. Two draft "EVA Intake Roadmap" rows (`a89b078b`, `8ffa7fdf`) were created 2026-07-17 by two separate Solomon `/distill` runs BEFORE the now-shipped single-writer guard (`SD-LEO-INFRA-DISTILL-ROADMAP-SINGLE-001`) landed. `scripts/one-off/archive-duplicate-roadmaps.mjs` archives them via a reversible `status='archived'` UPDATE (never a DELETE) — dry-run by default, gated behind `--apply`, with a hardcoded 2-id allowlist (never a dynamic `title=` match, so a future unrelated row can't be caught by accident) and a fail-closed referrer precondition built into the script itself (aborts with zero writes if any row in `roadmap_baseline_snapshots`, `loop_registry`, or `strategic_directives_v2.metadata` references either target id or their 9 child waves). A pre-existing, already-archived March 2026 row and the active LEO Roadmap are both explicitly left untouched.
  - **Verified twice, independently, before any write**: the worker's own pre-EXEC check and a separate LEAD-TO-PLAN VALIDATION sub-agent pass both confirmed all 1080 `roadmap_wave_items` under the 2 draft roadmaps' 9 waves are pure `youtube`/`todoist` intake-table references (every `source_id` resolves into a real `eva_youtube_intake`/`eva_todoist_intake` row) with zero unique authored content and zero `promoted_to_sd_key` — the VALIDATION pass caught and corrected an item-count estimation error in the worker's own draft PRD (1000 claimed vs. 1080 actual), reinforcing that adversarial review catches real gaps even on small, apparently-trivial SDs. A same-day Quick-Fix proposal describing this exact cleanup was found in `.prd-payloads/` but confirmed never materialized as a live `quick_fixes` row — no duplicate in-flight work.
  - **PLAN-TO-EXEC TESTING found a real test-coverage gap**: the original test plan covered the archive/verify happy path but had no test for the dry-run-makes-zero-writes safety property or the fail-closed abort-on-referrer-found precondition. Both were added (as new scenarios) before EXEC wrote the script, and the resulting `checkReferrers()` function is independently unit-tested (6 tests) for exactly those paths.
  - **Verification**: 48 tests passing in the roadmap test directory (6 new, 42 pre-existing — including the `resolveCanonicalRoadmap()` exactly-one-active-roadmap invariant test, unaffected since the target rows were already `draft`, not `active`). Applied live: post-archive active count = 1 (LEO Roadmap only). EXEC-TO-PLAN TESTING and SECURITY both independently re-verified the live DB state matched the script exactly, with no injection risk and a non-bypassable id allowlist. `/heal` scored 100/100. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 95, PLAN-TO-EXEC 95, EXEC-TO-PLAN 95, PLAN-TO-LEAD 97, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 99.
- **Op-co switch-on automation, Child D (final): wires the switch-on gate into the real PLAN-TO-EXEC decision path + applies it to op-co-A** - PR #6236 (SD-LEO-INFRA-INTELLIGENT-SWITCH-AUTOMATION-001-D)
  - **What shipped**: the 4th and final child of the switch-on automation orchestrator (A: classifier + policy table, PR #6220; B: `authorizeSwitchOn` precheck gate, PR #6223; C: 7 mandatory prechecks, PR #6224 — all previously built-but-unwired). Child D is the integration layer: `scripts/modules/handoff/executors/plan-to-exec/gates/exec-boundary-hold.js` gains a `metadata.switchon_action`-gated branch that calls `authorizeSwitchOn` (B) + `runSwitchOnPrechecks` (C) before falling back to the pre-existing manual-park WAIT — a reversible, precheck-green verdict auto-clears the EXEC hold; anything else (never-auto, consequential, unknown, or an evaluator throw) fires a new one-tap chairman decision packet (`lib/switch-automation/switchon-decision-packet.js`: a durable `chairman_decisions` console record via the existing `recordPendingDecision` pipeline, plus a best-effort SMS nudge that self-degrades to console-only for genuinely irreversible/HIGH-consequence actions) and returns the same WAIT shape — byte-identical to today when `switchon_action` is absent, proven by the pre-existing `exec-boundary-hold.test.js` passing unmodified. Applied concretely to `SD-FDBK-ENH-EHG-OPERATING-COMPANY-001-A` (provision the live venture surface) via a `--dry-run`/`--apply`-gated one-off script: its blanket `requires_human_action`/`do_not_auto_dispatch` fence — which blocked even LEAD/PLAN work despite its own fence text saying "Reversible LEAD/PLAN may proceed" — is converted to the phase-scoped `exec_boundary_hold`, with every legacy fence marker (5 keys, including a self-contradictory `irreversible_exec_chairman_gated:true` alongside `requires_human_action:false`) archived into `metadata.switchon_migrated_from_legacy_fence` rather than left live. Siblings -B/-C deliberately untouched — -B is chairman-PARKED for an unrelated demand-gating decision the coordinator had already once wrongly unfenced and had to re-fence.
  - **Four independent adversarial review rounds, each catching real gaps before merge**: LEAD-TO-PLAN VALIDATION (82/100) found the PRD's own FR-1 example omitted the `inRole` field `classifyDecision` requires for an EXECUTE verdict, scoped the reversible-auto-clear path as a stub-tested-only capability (no op-co component is actually reversible yet), and caught a wrong JSONB idempotency-dedup path in FR-2's own description. PLAN-TO-EXEC TESTING (88/100) then found the PRD's own FR-2 example call to `recordPendingDecision()` omitted its required first `supabase` argument (would have silently no-op'd every decision packet), and corrected an architectural assumption — sibling PLAN-TO-EXEC gates use constructor-injected `supabase` clients, not `ctx.supabase`, requiring a one-line change to `plan-to-exec/index.js`'s gate registration. Both review rounds fixed real spec bugs baked into the PRD *before* any code was written. Post-implementation, EXEC-TO-PLAN TESTING (96/100) independently re-ran the full 200+-test suite and re-verified the live op-co-A migration; EXEC-TO-PLAN SECURITY (92/100) traced `classifySwitchOn → authorizeSwitchOn → gate` end-to-end confirming no metadata-manipulation path can auto-clear a NEVER-AUTO action, and found one LOW finding — the migration script wasn't idempotent against an accidental re-run — fixed with a one-line guard before merge.
  - **Incidental fix**: found and fixed a genuinely pre-existing, unrelated bug in Child C's `migrations-tier1.test.js` while working in the same test directory — its SQL comment-stripping regex `--.*$` silently failed to match anything on a line ending in `\r` (Windows CRLF), since `.` never matches `\r` (a JS regex line-terminator character) and `$` without the `m` flag only anchors at the true end of the whole string. Confirmed pre-existing via `git stash` before fixing.
  - **Verification**: 200+ tests passing across the switch-automation and plan-to-exec suites (0 failures), including 9 new tests for the gate's switch-on branch, 7 for the decision-packet dispatcher, and 7 for the migration logic against the real live op-co-A metadata shape. `/heal` scored 100/100. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 95, PLAN-TO-EXEC 100, EXEC-TO-PLAN 93, PLAN-TO-LEAD 97, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 99. Closes out the parent `SD-LEO-INFRA-INTELLIGENT-SWITCH-AUTOMATION-001` orchestrator (A/B/C/D all merged).
- **Op-co switch-on automation, Child A: reversibility classifier + chairman-gated NEVER-AUTO policy table + predicate evaluator** - PR #6220 (SD-LEO-INFRA-INTELLIGENT-SWITCH-AUTOMATION-001-A)
  - **What shipped**: first of 4 children under the `SD-LEO-INFRA-INTELLIGENT-SWITCH-AUTOMATION-001` orchestrator (decomposed from a single `infrastructure` SD per an independent VALIDATION recommendation — the scope carries constitutional weight, since it governs when op-co switch-on actions are allowed to auto-proceed vs. require the chairman). Child A delivers the foundation the other three children build on: (1) `lib/switch-automation/reversibility-classifier.js`'s `classifySwitchOn()`, a 3-verdict (`reversible`/`consequential`/`unknown`) classifier that adapts (without mutating) the existing `lib/adam/execute-vs-escalate.js` rubric, with an 18-entry `NEVER_AUTO_CLASSES` list (venture-gate-binding-flip, live-venture-deploy, live-money-enablement, live-payment-account-creation, dns-mutation, public-launch, venture-kill, gate-config-change, kill-switch-machinery, policy-ratchet-self-reference, etc.) that always wins regardless of other inputs, and fails closed to `unknown` on any missing required field; (2) `database/migrations/20260718_chairman_switchon_policy_STAGED.sql`, a chairman-gated `chairman_switchon_policy` table shipped STAGED (mirrors the `sms_decision_class_whitelist_STAGED.sql` precedent) — RLS enabled with a chairman-only SELECT policy, deliberately no insert/update/delete policy, and a DB-hard `REVOKE INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE ... FROM anon, authenticated, service_role` ratchet so even `service_role` (which bypasses RLS but not GRANT/REVOKE) cannot widen the policy — only the table owner via the chairman-apply ceremony can; (3) `database/migrations/20260718_release_condition_predicate.sql` (additive, non-breaking `hold_state_contract_violations.release_condition_predicate` JSONB column) plus `lib/governance/release-condition-predicate.js`'s pure `evaluate(predicate, state)`, which fails closed on any unrecognized predicate type or missing state rather than defaulting permissive.
  - **Two adversarial review rounds, each catching real gaps before merge**: pre-EXEC TESTING review found 3 PRD gaps — the "unknown" verdict's required-field/precedence rules were underspecified (added explicit enumeration + precedence description), the ratchet-guard test scenario was unrunnable against a never-applied STAGED migration (split into a testable static-file-lint form now, with the runtime ephemeral-DB privilege probe explicitly deferred via an `it.todo` to the chairman-apply ceremony rather than silently dropped), and the predicate evaluator was specified as "pure" while implicitly reading live state (respecified as `evaluate(predicate, state)` with state caller-injected). Post-implementation SECURITY review then found a genuine compliance gap: the original NEVER-AUTO list didn't verbatim-cover the SD's own GUARDRAIL-1 acceptance criterion, which mandates 3 named examples — DNS mutation had zero corresponding class. Fixed immediately (not deferred, since GUARDRAIL-1 is mandatory) by adding `live-venture-deploy`, `live-payment-account-creation`, `dns-mutation`, and a dedicated parity regression test asserting each is verbatim present.
  - **Verification**: 41 tests passing across 3 new test files (23 for the classifier, including a parametrized loop over all 18 NEVER-AUTO classes; 7 static-file-lint tests for the STAGED migration's RLS/REVOKE structure plus the GUARDRAIL-1 parity assertion; 7 for the predicate evaluator), plus 1 explicit `it.todo` documenting the chairman-ceremony-deferred runtime probe. Change surface is exactly 5 new files — no existing code modified. `/heal` scored 100/100 (self-corrected a real chairman-mandated compliance gap under adversarial review rather than shipping silently non-compliant). LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 99%.

### Bugfix
- **Retro-flagged E2E evidence gap on SMS-relay user stories, fixed at the root (STORIES sub-agent boilerplate for no-UI features)** - PR #6216 (SD-LEO-FIX-RETRO-ACTION-ITEMS-003)
  - **What shipped**: a retro action item auto-promoted from SD-LEO-FEAT-SMS-INBOUND-RELAY-001's own retrospective flagged an unverified E2E-coverage requirement. Investigation found the real defect: all 5 `user_stories` rows for that already-shipped feature (US-001..US-005) carried STORIES-sub-agent-generated boilerplate `acceptance_criteria` — generic UI-navigation/form-submission language ("the user has navigated to the area...") for a feature that is a backend Twilio webhook relay with **no UI at all** — and their `e2e_test_path` pointed at unrelated, pre-existing spec files (`accessibility-venture-creation.spec.ts`, `board-governance.spec.ts`, `api-coverage-audit.spec.ts`) with zero SMS/relay content. `e2e_test_status='created'` and `e2e_test_last_run=null` on all 5 meant no story had ever had verified passing evidence linked to it, despite the feature having shipped with real coverage. Fixed via `scripts/one-off/fix-sms-relay-story-evidence.mjs`, which repointed each story at its actual covering evidence (`tests/unit/chairman/sms-bridge.test.js`, `tests/unit/webhooks/twilio-sms.test.js`, the `ehg` repo's `tests/unit/sms-relay/*`, and `scripts/security/sms-relay-redteam.js`), ran that evidence for real (35/35 tests passing, independently re-verified by the TESTING sub-agent), and stamped genuine `e2e_test_status`/`e2e_test_last_run` from the actual run rather than rubber-stamping. This SD's own 3 auto-generated `user_stories` carried the identical boilerplate defect — a self-referential confirmation the gap is systemic, not isolated to one feature — and were fixed the same way.
  - **Root cause, not just symptom**: the STORIES sub-agent's boilerplate-generation pipeline doesn't distinguish backend/no-UI features from UI features, and the downstream gates that consume `e2e_test_path`/`e2e_test_status` (`lib/sub-agents/testing/phases/phase4-evidence.js`, `plan-to-lead/gates/acceptance-criteria-validation.js`) accept any truthy path string with no content/relevance verification — so nothing in the pipeline ever catches a wrong or boilerplate reference. Retrospective (id `07ce73e2-19d1-47ea-a672-596a12d5bb5d`, quality 90/100) captures this as a fleet-wide action item: sweep other backend SDs for the same defect class, and add content-relevance checking to the consuming gates.
  - **Harness bug found and worked around, not silently bypassed**: `GATE2_IMPLEMENTATION_FIDELITY`'s "unresolved ambiguities" preflight check false-positived on this SD twice (once at EXEC-TO-PLAN, again at PLAN-TO-LEAD's internal Gate-2 re-check) — it matched two completely unrelated directories (`test-venture`, `test-cicd`: generic Vite/React scaffold projects with zero references to this SD's key anywhere in their tree) and flagged vendored TypeScript/Babel compiler-diagnostic strings containing the word "ambiguous" as blocking markers. Confirmed via direct `grep -ril` investigation before acting; used the documented `--bypass-validation --bypass-reason` path both times (audit-logged, CI's `Bypass Validation Result`/`LEO Protocol Bypass Detection` checks both passed), and filed a `gate-bug` signal to the coordinator with the full false-positive evidence rather than silently working around it.
  - **Verification**: TESTING sub-agent independently re-ran the evidence (35/35 passing) and confirmed the change surface was exactly one new file (no application/relay code touched); SECURITY sub-agent confirmed no credentials or secret material in the new acceptance-criteria text and no posture regression on the shipped feature. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 95, PLAN-TO-EXEC 94, EXEC-TO-PLAN 95 (bypass), PLAN-TO-LEAD 93 (bypass), LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 95.

## 2026-07-17

### Security
- **Chairman SMS bridge: untrusted public relay carve-out, closes a service-role-on-public-host exposure** - PR #6154, PR #6165, rickfelix/ehg#761 (SD-LEO-FEAT-SMS-INBOUND-RELAY-001)
  - **What shipped**: chairman-requested (per Solomon security verdict f3c511c5). The inbound half of `SD-LEO-FEAT-TWO-WAY-CHAIRMAN-001`'s chairman SMS bridge (`api/webhooks/twilio-sms.js`) verified the Twilio signature then always resolved decisions in-process with a SERVICE-ROLE Supabase client — unsafe to expose on a public host, since a marketing-site or dependency compromise could inject arbitrary chairman decisions. Carved the untrusted public surface into an isolated deploy unit (`ehg` repo's `sms-relay/`, meant to run as its own Vercel project on `hooks.execholdings.ai`, zero service-role credential, zero dependencies) that INSERT-only relays candidate replies into a new EHG_Engineer staging table (`sms_relay_staging`) via a SECURITY DEFINER RPC. The already-shipped trusted resolver (`lib/chairman/sms-bridge.js` `handleInboundSmsReply`) is reused unchanged as the consumer, with two additions: ambiguous-reply rejection (2+ simultaneously-eligible pending candidates) and a persistent auto-suspend circuit breaker (`sms_inbound_suspensions`, survives past the existing 60-minute rolling rate-limit window). `api/webhooks/twilio-sms.js` gained a `SMS_RELAY_CUTOVER_COMPLETE` flag that decommissions its direct-write path without deleting it — instant rollback via unsetting the flag.
  - **Same-session security-review finding, closed before merge**: the EXEC-TO-PLAN SECURITY sub-agent found the anon-key EXECUTE grant on the staging RPC restricted *which* function could be called but not *who* called it — since the anon key may already be public (shared Supabase project backing a browser-facing app), anyone holding it could have called the RPC directly and forged a candidate reply, bypassing the relay's HMAC verification entirely (`signature_valid` was hardcoded `true` inside the RPC with no caller check). Closed same-session with `p_relay_secret`, a second factor validated against an RLS-deny-all singleton table (`sms_relay_secret`), so anon-key possession alone is insufficient.
  - **PLAN-phase TESTING sub-agent caught real PRD ambiguities before EXEC started**: the original `test_scenarios` referenced a client-typed "nonce" that doesn't exist in the actual resolver design (replies are free text, correlated by phone+TTL), an undefined "batch reply rejected" behavior the resolver didn't implement, and an inconsistency between a spoofed-signature test scenario and the staging table's `signature_valid` column semantics. All three resolved by patching the PRD's FR-3/test_scenarios before implementation began.
  - **Scripted red-team acceptance gate**: `scripts/security/sms-relay-redteam.js` (`npm run security:sms-relay-redteam`) is a committed, two-tier gate — `--target=local` (default) runs the full local/CI scenario suite across both repos with no live deployment needed; `--target=deployed` prints the manual pre-pilot checklist for the scenarios that need the actual `hooks.execholdings.ai` deployment (end-to-end reply resolution, proxy/rewrite-mismatch signature rejection, and RPC-grants verification against a live restricted-role Postgres connection).
  - **Verification**: 34 new/modified unit tests across both repos (`tests/unit/chairman/sms-bridge.test.js`, `tests/unit/webhooks/twilio-sms.test.js`, `tests/unit/sms-relay/*` in `ehg`), all passing. VALIDATION, Explore, DESIGN, DATABASE, STORIES, SECURITY, RISK, TESTING sub-agents all ran with fresh evidence. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 96, PLAN-TO-EXEC 87, EXEC-TO-PLAN 94, PLAN-TO-LEAD 95.
- **Block phantom test-session claims + reap in the sweep** - PR #6155 (SD-LEO-INFRA-BLOCK-TEST-SESSION-001)
  - **What shipped**: `claim_sd()` — the SECURITY DEFINER RPC every fleet worker uses to claim SD/QF work — never validated that the calling `p_session_id` had a live `claude_sessions` row; its terminal `UPDATE claude_sessions` silently no-oped on a missing row while the paired `strategic_directives_v2`/`quick_fixes` UPDATE ran unconditionally, so a phantom/never-registered session (witnessed live incident: `test-session-nswcf-fenced`, zero rows in `claude_sessions`) claimed two real SDs. Fixed with a claim-time existence guard immediately after the advisory lock (mirrors the existing `session_not_found` idiom already used by `release_session()`), applied to production via the token-gated `apply-migration.js --prod-deploy` ceremony. A new `reapPhantomSessionClaims()` pass in `scripts/stale-session-sweep.cjs` reaps any already-leaked phantom claim, cross-signal-guarded (checks `claiming_session_id`, `active_session_id`, and `claude_sessions.sd_key` before reaping, so it never false-releases a claim a *different* live session legitimately holds), race-guarded on release, audited via `session_lifecycle_events`.
  - **Scope correction found during LEAD**: the SD's own scope text suggested an additional `test-session-*-fenced` regex fence. Dropped after reading `tests/database/seat-busy-fence.test.js` directly — it deliberately registers a real `claude_sessions` row for that exact literal session id to exercise unrelated seat-busy-fence/checkin logic via the real `worker-checkin.cjs` CLI; the regex would have rejected that legitimately-registered session and corrupted the test's intent. The general NOT-EXISTS check alone is durable (the witnessed incident session had zero rows) and doesn't collide with it.
  - **Verification**: 8 new tests (`tests/database/claim-sd-phantom-session-guard.test.js`, `tests/integration/phantom-session-reap.integration.test.js`) pass against the live DB; 20-test regression sweep across `claim-sd-validate-exists`/`claim-sd-terminal-status`/`claim-sd-cross-table`/`claim-sd-refuse-live-foreign` plus the specifically-protected `seat-busy-fence` suite (2/2) all pass. Deep-tier adversarial review: no CRITICAL/WARNING findings. RISK, DATABASE, TESTING (LEAD+EXEC), VALIDATION (LEAD+VERIFY), Explore, SECURITY, REGRESSION sub-agents all PASS/CONDITIONAL_PASS. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 95, PLAN-TO-EXEC 96, EXEC-TO-PLAN 94, PLAN-TO-LEAD 97, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 99.

### Infrastructure
- **Fable-5 golden-task baseline seal attestation — verify the window-critical corpus before Fable access closes** - PR #6206 (SD-LEO-INFRA-TIME-CRITICAL-SEAL-001)
  - **What shipped**: chairman intel flagged Fable-5 access as closing ~2026-07-19, making the model's golden-task answers (`feedback.category='model_capability_baseline'`, suite `FABLE5-BASELINE-2026-07-16`) the only window-dependent, ungeneratable-after-the-fact artifact in the baseline harness — grading itself is deliberately deferred to the cross-model eval harness / Opus-5 first run (`docs/design/solomon-fable-capability-grounding.md` Part 4), so the time-critical task was narrowly to attest the sealed corpus is complete, not to grade it. Added a pure verifier (`lib/eval/verify-baseline-seal.mjs` `verifyBaselineSeal()`) asserting all 10 answer keys and all 30 sealed runs (10 tasks × 3 effort tiers) are present with `content_hash`, `task_text`, `task_id`, and the load-bearing `fable5_answer`, plus a thin CLI (`scripts/eval/verify-fable5-baseline-seal.mjs`, `npm run eval:verify-fable5-seal`) that reads the corpus and prints a machine-readable `SEALED`/`INCOMPLETE` verdict. Missing token/wall-clock telemetry on the low/medium effort tiers is reported as a non-blocking warning by design — backfilling it would require re-running Fable-5 and changing the sealed answers, breaking the very seal being verified.
  - **Salvaged rather than restarted**: picked up mid-build from a prior session that had lost its claim, with a worktree 8 commits behind `origin/main` and pre-existing staged work. Rather than discard and rebuild, ground-truthed the actual deadline-bearing artifact directly against the DB first (confirmed the corpus was already fully sealed), fast-forward merged `origin/main` (no conflicts), and continued from the salvaged implementation.
  - **Two full rounds of independent adversarial `/ship` review, each catching real bugs**: round 1 found a CRITICAL completeness-masking defect — total-count and shape-coverage checks alone can be fooled, since a duplicate `answer_key` row for one task can silently offset another task's total absence (two sibling tasks often share a shape), and total run-count checks miss a task with zero runs and no answer_key mismatch signal. Fixed with per-task-id duplicate detection plus a bidirectional `answer_key`↔`sealed_run` task-id set-compare (verified non-manifesting on live data: 10 unique key task_ids, 10 unique run task_ids, no duplicates), with 2 new tests reproducing the exact masking scenarios. Round 1 also fixed a Windows libuv `UV_HANDLE_CLOSING` exit-code corruption (a `process.exit()` immediately after a still-closing Supabase HTTP handle crashed the CLI *after* printing the correct verdict, corrupting the real exit code to 127 — a CI step keying on `$?` would misread a genuine `SEALED` result as failure) on both the success and DB-error paths, switching to `process.exitCode`. Round 2, run via the `Workflow` tool with two independent parallel reviewer lenses (completeness-logic, security/exit-code), found the identity checks asserted uniqueness/pairing but never that `task_id` itself was a real non-falsy value (closed with explicit `missing task_id` checks on both key and run sides, 2 new tests), and a `.catch()` handler that set `process.exitCode` *after* its own `console.error` call — reordered so the exit code is locked in before any I/O that could itself throw.
  - **PLAN-phase SECURITY finding**: the effort-tier-coverage map was keyed by a plain object on an externally-sourced `task_id` — a task_id of `'__proto__'` would collide with `Object.prototype` instead of behaving as a normal key. Converted to a `Map`. A separate redaction regression test seeds sentinel values into every sensitive field (`answer_key`, `task_text`, `fable5_answer`) and asserts none ever appear in `JSON.stringify()` of the verifier's result, on both the `SEALED` and `INCOMPLETE` paths (the human-readable `reasons` array is a common inadvertent leak vector for exactly this class of check).
  - **Verification**: 12/12 unit tests (`lib/eval/__tests__/verify-baseline-seal.test.js`) covering the happy path, every completeness dimension, both masking traps, and the redaction regression. Live CLI run against the production corpus returned `SEALED` with exit code 0.
- **Post-merge automation vs worker LEAD-FINAL claim window — race fix** - PR #6195 (SD-LEO-FIX-POST-MERGE-AUTOMATION-001)
  - **What shipped**: coordinator-verified recurrence (x2, one worker) of post-merge automation (`scripts/post-merge-handoff-orchestrator.js`) racing a worker's own `LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL` invocation against the same SD — root-caused via live `leo_handoff_executions` evidence across 4+ SDs (duplicate accepted rows + interleaved `NO_CLAIM` rejections within a 1-2 minute window). Two independent defects: the claim-validity gate (`evaluateClaimCheckForHandoff`) was blind to `sd.status`, treating "unclaimed because the SD just completed and released its own claim" identically to a genuinely foreign/abandoned claim (the 2026-06-12 ghost-completion class this gate exists to catch); and the terminal `strategic_directives_v2` completion UPDATE was unconditional, letting two invocations that both passed the claim gate both believe they won. Fixed with a status-aware exemption (`sd.status==='completed'` now routes to the existing idempotent already-completed path instead of hard-blocking) scoped ONLY to `LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL` (a same-session security review caught the initial version was reachable by every handoff type), plus a CAS-guarded terminal UPDATE (`.eq('status','pending_approval')`, new `cas-completion.js`) with loser-side pre-insert cleanup by exact row id.
  - **Two-round deep-tier adversarial `/ship` review, each round catching something real**: round 1 found the CAS-miss branch assumed any status change away from `pending_approval` meant a peer completed the SD, and would fabricate a false completion record for any other cause (cancellation, manual reset) — fixed to verify `freshSd.status === 'completed'` before reconciling, otherwise rejecting with a distinct `CAS_MISS_UNEXPECTED_STATUS` code. Round 2 confirmed the fix clean; a second, pre-existing, out-of-scope TOCTOU on the (unmodified) canonical `sd_phase_handoffs` check-then-insert was independently flagged by both the EXEC-phase TESTING sub-agent and this adversarial pass, and tracked as a documented follow-up rather than silently deferred.
  - **Verification**: 25 new/modified unit tests across 3 files (`handoff-claim-gate.test.js` 6-case `sdStatus` matrix, new `lead-final-approval-cas-race.test.js` shared-stateful-fake-DB race simulation verified red-before/green-after, new `base-executor-claim-gate-fresh-read.test.js` covering the BaseExecutor wiring + security scoping). Zero regressions across the full `tests/unit/handoff/` suite (791 tests) and the full `npm run test:unit` run (28,294 passed; 2 unrelated pre-existing failures, one already root-caused this session as an `.env`-hermeticity gap). TESTING (PLAN+EXEC) and SECURITY sub-agents both CONDITIONAL_PASS with findings addressed same-session; RETRO PASS (quality 100/100). Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 96, PLAN-TO-EXEC 95, EXEC-TO-PLAN 98, PLAN-TO-LEAD 97, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 96.
- **Fleet account-identity awareness — detect /login account switches, attribute limit events** - PR #6177 (SD-LEO-INFRA-FLEET-ACCOUNT-IDENTITY-001)
  - **What shipped**: chairman-witnessed gap — a scheduled fleet run around a 10:30am session-limit reset silently stopped applying the moment the chairman switched Claude Code accounts mid-session via `/login` (machine-global, switches ALL sessions on the box), and nothing in the harness noticed. Added a whitelist-only reader (`lib/fleet/account-identity.cjs`) surfacing exactly `{email, orgName, accountUuid8}` from `~/.claude.json`'s `oauthAccount` (never any of its ~16 other sub-fields or the config's ~87 other top-level keys), wired an `acct=<email>` token into `adam-quiet-tick.mjs`/`coordinator-quiet-tick.mjs`/`fleet-dashboard.cjs`, stamped identity onto `spawn-executor-core.cjs` diagnostics, and added debounced `ACCOUNT_SWITCH` detection (cold-start-silent, fires exactly once per genuine change, reusing the existing `detectSalientDelta`-style state-diff pattern) sending one coordinator notice via the existing `insertCoordinationRow()` choke point. Retires the "Fleet = ONE account" blind-spot class — the constraint stays true, now it's OBSERVED, not assumed.
  - **Pre-EXEC test-plan review caught 3 real gaps before any code was written**: the PLAN-TO-EXEC TESTING sub-agent found the leak-safety test was unimplementable against the real, secret-free config file (required an injection-seam addition to the reader's contract), the reused debounce pattern fires `changed:true` on a null prior state (would have spuriously alerted on every first tick after deploy/restart — required an explicit cold-start-silent contract), and no fail-soft test existed for a missing/malformed config. All 3 closed by amending the PRD before implementation began.
  - **Two rounds of adversarial review, each catching something the prior pass missed**: an EXEC-phase workflow-driven 3-lens review found unsanitized whitelist fields could forge log lines via embedded control/ANSI-escape characters if the on-disk config were ever tampered with (fixed via a `sanitizeField()` helper), and a debounce-regression test gap (fixed). A separate, independent deep-tier `/ship` review then found the sanitizer's control-character range was incomplete (C1 codes 0x80-0x9F, including 8-bit CSI, were untouched — widened the regex) and that the `ACCOUNT_SWITCH` notification's baseline advanced unconditionally before delivery was confirmed, silently and permanently losing the switch signal on a coordinator-lookup or DB-insert failure — fixed so the baseline only advances on confirmed delivery, so an undelivered switch keeps retrying every tick until it lands.
  - **Verification**: 11 new unit tests (`tests/unit/fleet/account-identity.test.js`), zero regressions across a 106-file/1217-test sweep (`tests/unit/fleet/`, `tests/unit/coordinator/`, `tests/unit/adam/`) aside from one pre-existing, unrelated test-hermeticity gap in a different SD's test file (flagged separately, not caused by this work). VALIDATION, Explore, TESTING (LEAD+EXEC), SECURITY sub-agents all PASS. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 97, PLAN-TO-EXEC 96, EXEC-TO-PLAN 95, PLAN-TO-LEAD 97, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 99.
- **Multi-session claim gate now reads the authoritative claim owner instead of a heartbeat view (recurred-family fix)** - PR #6164 (SD-LEO-INFRA-MULTI-SESSION-CLAIM-001)
  - **What shipped**: `GATE_MULTI_SESSION_CLAIM_CONFLICT` (`scripts/modules/handoff/gates/multi-session-claim-gate.js`'s `validateMultiSessionClaim()`, which runs before every LEAD/PLAN/EXEC handoff to block duplicate concurrent work) derived claim ownership from the `v_active_sessions` heartbeat view instead of `strategic_directives_v2.claiming_session_id` — the authoritative Surface A written by `claim_sd()` and already used correctly by the adjacent `assertValidClaim()` gate. An unrelated dead peer session holding a stale `sd_key` stamp with a fresh-looking heartbeat could false-block the legitimate claim owner's own handoff, witnessed live 2026-07-17 01:57Z and logged as a deferred harness-backlog item in the 2026-07-16 `SD-FDBK-INFRA-FIX-GATE-SUBAGENT-001` entry above (4th witness of `PAT-LEO-INFRA-WRITER-CONSUMER-ASYMMETRY-001`). Rewrote the gate to read Surface A first, then delegate liveness/staleness decisions to the same hardened primitives `assertValidClaim()` already uses (`lib/claim-validity-gate.js`'s `ownerIsDeadByLiveness`/`shouldReleaseStaleOwner`, with `isOwnerProcessAlive` newly exported for reuse, plus `lib/fleet/silence-cap.cjs`'s `isWithinArmedSilenceWindow`), while preserving the pre-existing same-conversation carve-out and DENY-on-ambiguity fallthrough-to-BLOCK.
  - **Recurred-family rule applied**: a prior fix (`SD-LEO-FIX-FIX-MULTI-SESSION-001`) had already addressed a related facet of this same gate, yet this Surface-A/Surface-B divergence recurred afterward — so per the recurred-family rule, a live-DB e2e acceptance test (not just mocked units) was required and added: `tests/integration/multi-session-claim-gate-surface-a.integration.test.js` seeds real `strategic_directives_v2` + `claude_sessions` rows reproducing the exact witnessed scenario (rightful owner not blocked by the phantom peer) plus the inverse no-regression case (a genuinely live foreign claim still blocks).
  - **Deep-tier adversarial review caught two real (fixed) findings, confirmed clean on the third pass**: round 1 found the owner-row `claude_sessions` lookup silently discarded its Supabase error, unlike the Surface A query above it — fixed by surfacing the error in the gate's `warnings`. Round 2 found the same error was still dropped on a different exit path (the BLOCK branch, reachable when the read errors but the owner's PID is independently alive) — fixed so both reachable exit paths surface it consistently. Round 3 confirmed clean.
  - **Verification**: 29 tests (15 rewritten unit + 12 unit + 2 live-DB e2e) pass; 102-test regression sweep across `tests/unit/claim/` and `tests/unit/session-writer/` clean. VALIDATION, Explore, TESTING (LEAD+EXEC), SECURITY, RETRO sub-agents all PASS. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 95, PLAN-TO-EXEC 98, EXEC-TO-PLAN 94, PLAN-TO-LEAD 97, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 99.

### Bugfix
- **Batch eva_scheduler_metrics writes on the scheduler-tick path** - PR #6201 (SD-LEO-FIX-EVA-SCHEDULER-METRICS-001)
  - **What shipped**: `eva_scheduler_metrics` grew ~110k rows/day. Grounding found retention was already delivered by a prior SD (`SD-REFILL-00LHUVME`) — a live `RETENTION_POLICIES` entry (90-day hot window) enforced by a weekly GHA cron — verified live against the DB (oldest row 37 days old, correctly configured, just not yet age-triggered). The unaddressed gap was the write path: `EvaMasterScheduler._emitMetric()` inserted one row per call across 12 per-tick call sites. Added `lib/eva/metrics-writer.js` (`MetricsWriter`), which buffers rows and flushes them as bulk `insert()` calls on a size (20 rows) or time (5s) trigger; `EvaMasterScheduler.stop()` now awaits a final flush on graceful shutdown so no buffered metric is lost. 4 other low-frequency direct-insert call sites (`domain-handler.js`, `okr-monthly-handler.js`, `okr-mid-month-review.js`) were intentionally left unbatched — not meaningful contributors to the growth rate.
  - **Explore-review finding closed same-session**: batching a bulk array insert means one FK-violating row (e.g. a metric for a since-deleted venture — `eva_scheduler_metrics.venture_id` has no `ON DELETE CASCADE`) could roll back an entire batch of otherwise-good rows, a new failure-correlation mode the pre-batching single-row-insert code didn't have. Fixed with a row-by-row retry fallback in `MetricsWriter.flush()` so only the genuinely bad row is lost.
  - **CI caught a real regression before merge**: `MetricsWriter`'s constructor initially threw if `supabase`/`table` were missing, but `lib/eva/rounds-scheduler.js` instantiates a module-level `EvaMasterScheduler` singleton without a DB client for registration-only use — eagerly imported by `lib/eva/event-bus/event-router.js` and transitively by ~59 test files, all of which failed at import time. Fixed by making construction lenient (matching the pre-existing `this.supabase = deps.supabase` possibly-undefined contract); `flush()` already failed soft if a write were attempted with no client configured.
  - **Verification**: `lib/eva/metrics-writer.js` (new, 14 unit tests) + updated `tests/unit/eva-master-scheduler.test.js` metric-emission assertions for the batched-array `insert()` shape, plus a new `stop()`-flushes-buffered-metrics regression test. TESTING and SECURITY sub-agents (EXEC phase) both PASS. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 96, PLAN-TO-EXEC 95, EXEC-TO-PLAN 98, PLAN-TO-LEAD 98, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 97.

## 2026-07-16

### Features
- **Chairman-designated high-consequence stage-gates now actually BLOCK the venture** - PR #6104 (SD-LEO-FEAT-MAKE-HIGH-CONSEQUENCE-001)
  - **What shipped**: chairman-delegated 2026-07-14 ("operate autonomously, make high-consequence gates bind"). `chairman_decisions.blocking` existed and already drove escalation email priority + SLA exemption + queue sort order, but never actually held venture advancement — a `blocking=true` pending decision and a `blocking=false` advisory one let the venture through identically. `venture_stages.is_high_consequence` (new, chairman-configurable, independent of `gate_type`/`review_mode` — e.g. can mark a `gate_type='none'` stage like a first live-money/launch stage that has no gate today) now drives two things: every mint site in `lib/eva/stage-execution-worker.js` sets `blocking=true` and forces minting past the pre-existing `stage_creates_decision` self-skip, and both venture-advancement chokepoints (SQL RPC `fn_advance_venture_stage`, JS daemon `_advanceStage`) HOLD while that row is pending — fail-closed on evaluator error (unlike the 3 pre-existing backstops, which fail open for availability), behind a `LEO_HIGH_CONSEQUENCE_GATES_ENABLED` kill-switch.
  - **Adversarial review caught the feature shipping inert, twice**: a Deep-tier `/ship` review (mandatory for this PR's migration-touching diff) found the first cut was inert for its own headline case — nothing ever minted the blocking row for a stage that wasn't already kill/promotion/review-gated, because the autonomy model auto-approved plain gates away before any mint call was reached. Fixed by making the review-mode block and `_handleChairmanGate` trigger on `isHighConsequence` and bypass autonomy entirely. A second adversarial pass found the fix still incomplete — a third, independent auto-approve shortcut (the pending-decision canonical-RPC resolver) lacked the same guard, and a mint failure fell through to fail-open instead of fail-closed; both closed. A third pass confirmed the gap closed and verified the ordering guarantee with a live-code test. Two secondary bugs found along the way were also fixed: the JS chokepoint silently swallowed a Supabase `{error}` response instead of throwing into its own fail-closed catch, and `createOrReusePendingDecision`'s reuse path never synced `blocking` onto an already-pending decision when a stage was reclassified.
  - **Scope boundary (known, not silent)**: enforcement covers the two canonical chokepoints, matching every prior stage-gating feature's precedent. `lib/agents/venture-ceo/handlers.js`'s autonomous-agent path writes `current_lifecycle_stage` with no gate of any kind and is not yet covered — a pre-existing, already-censused bypass (`docs/architecture/stage-advancement-path-census.md` #16), tracked as a fast-follow candidate, not this SD's scope.
  - **Verification**: 6600+ unit tests + 9 real-DB integration tests, zero regressions across 3 rounds of fixes. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 96, PLAN-TO-EXEC 87, EXEC-TO-PLAN 93, PLAN-TO-LEAD 95, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 96.

### Infrastructure
- **Fix-effectiveness back-edge finally lit up: dark outcome-tracker.js wired to real data and real callers** - PR #6127 (SD-LEO-INFRA-FIX-RECURRENCE-REWIRING-001)
  - **What shipped**: `lib/learning/outcome-tracker.js` already contained a complete fix-effectiveness back-edge (`computeEffectiveness`/`recordSdCompleted` and `detectRecurrence`, built by `SD-LEO-ORCH-SELF-IMPROVING-LEO-001-C`) but it was entirely dark. FR-1: retabled the module (and `scripts/leo-analytics.js`) off the near-abandoned `leo_feedback` table (1 orphan row, zero writers) onto the live `feedback` table (8,815 rows), mapping `resolved_by_sd_id` to `feedback`'s actual `resolution_sd_id` column. FR-2: wired `detectRecurrence` (a jaccard-similarity matcher that had never fired — `outcome_signals` had 3,169 rows, all `sd_completion`, zero `pattern_recurrence`) via a new `feedback.created` event on the existing lightweight `vision-events.js` fire-and-forget bus, triggered from `emitFeedback`/`emitFeedbackBatch`'s insert path. FR-3: added `scripts/outcome-effectiveness-summary.mjs`, a live CLI over the previously-uncalled `getOutcomeSummary()`. FR-4: hooked `complete-quick-fix.js` into the tracker via a new `recordQfCompleted`, schema-safe because `outcome_signals`/`sd_effectiveness_metrics` carry a NOT NULL FK to `strategic_directives_v2` that a bare QF id could never satisfy.
  - **Adversarial review caught a real routing bug**: the deep-tier `/ship` review for PR #6127 found that escalated-QF routing sent those QFs exclusively to `recordSdCompleted` (which resolves feedback via `feedback.sd_id`), silently skipping the QF's actual linked feedback (`feedback.quick_fix_id` — a different linkage entirely). Fixed so `recordQfCompleted` always runs, with `recordSdCompleted` running additionally when the QF escalated. A secondary, unrelated bug was also caught and fixed in the same file: CI's schema-reference-lint (which checks a whole touched file, not just the diff) surfaced that `scripts/leo-analytics.js` had been querying a nonexistent `leo_vetting_outcomes.verdict` column (the real column is `outcome`) — the dashboard's Vetting Coverage section had been silently erroring.
  - **Known, deliberately-accepted gap**: ~40+ files insert into `feedback` directly, bypassing `emitFeedback`/`emitFeedbackBatch`, so FR-2's wiring covers the two canonical call sites only — documented in-code rather than silently over-claimed.
  - **Verification**: 7 new unit tests (`outcome-tracker-rewiring.test.js`, `outcome-tracker-hook.test.js`), zero regressions across the full suite (556+ files, 7100+ tests). FR-3 verified live against the DB post-retable: real pre=6/post=0/-100% effectiveness delta for a completed SD, replacing the prior all-zero garbage computed against the near-empty `leo_feedback`. Handoffs EXEC-TO-PLAN 94, PLAN-TO-LEAD 96, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 99.
- **LEO Roadmap wired as the live, self-maintaining plan of record** - PR #6112 (SD-LEO-INFRA-PLAN-OF-RECORD-LINKAGE-001)
  - **What shipped**: chairman-directed governance consolidation (2026-07-16, `strategic_roadmaps` active row `3aa2f3e2` ratified as the single plan of record). `lib/roadmap/roadmap-completion-stamp.js` + a new `lead-final-approval` completion hook flip `roadmap_wave_items.item_disposition` to `'promoted'` when a linked SD completes — previously only creation/promotion-time paths stamped `promoted_to_sd_key`, so completions via any other path left the roadmap permanently unstamped. `lib/roadmap/plan-check-status.js` (+ CLI `scripts/roadmap/plan-check-status.mjs`) now derives the chairman's PLAN CHECK slipped/done/next/committing sections directly from `roadmap_waves`+`roadmap_wave_items` JOINed against `strategic_directives_v2.status`, replacing the `adam_task_ledger` side-list (CLAUDE_ADAM.md's MECHANICS paragraph updated accordingly). `scripts/one-off/backfill-roadmap-completion-linkage.mjs` closes the historical backlog with a done-state-verified match (never a bare title guess).
  - **Scope discipline**: the PRD's original FR-3 (schedule the rung-progress rollup on a cadence) was dropped after a direct read of `.github/workflows/wave-progress-refresher.yml` confirmed it already runs on a live 6-hour cron, shipped by `SD-LEO-INFRA-ROADMAP-FOLD-SEAM-001` — a 25% scope reduction (LEAD Q8 deletion audit) rather than rebuilding already-shipped work.

A deep-tier adversarial `/ship` review then caught the backfill script's `isPlausibleMatch()` implementing only a bare title match despite its own docstring claiming temporal corroboration — fixed to require the linked SD's `completion_date` to postdate the roadmap item's `created_at`, and to never resurrect a deliberately-`'dropped'` item.

Live smoke test: `plan-check-status.mjs --json` against production correctly surfaced this session's own just-completed SDs under "done" within the 48h window. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 94, PLAN-TO-EXEC 94, PLAN-TO-LEAD 95, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 98.
- **Real `timeFromDefectToShippedFix` in the learning-moat gauge** - PR #6101 (SD-LEO-GEN-SATELLITE-LEARNING-SPEED-001)
  - **What shipped**: `lib/eva/learning-moat-gauge.js`'s `computeLearningMoatGauge()` previously left `timeFromDefectToShippedFix` permanently `null` — a documented, intentional placeholder pending real resolved-reflection data. Now computes it as the mean latency (hours, rounded to 1 decimal) between `created_at` and `resolution_date` across resolved (`resolution_date IS NOT NULL`) `traversal_reflection`-origin `issue_patterns` rows, while preserving the exact honest-null behavior and reason string when zero such rows exist (the current live state — no venture has completed a full 26-stage traversal yet). No schema change; both `created_at` and `resolution_date` already existed on `issue_patterns`.
  - **Dedup context**: this SD was a stale re-promotion of an already-completed satellite (`SD-LEO-ORCH-OPERATING-COMPANY-SPINE-001-E`, PR #5988); verified against `origin/main` that traversal-reflection emission, the gauge, the anti-Goodhart guard, and the capability ledger were already live, and rescoped to the one field the original SD's own doc comment named as a legitimate future follow-up.
  - **Verification**: 9/9 unit tests pass (`tests/unit/eva/learning-moat-gauge.test.js`), covering the honest-zero path, real computation, mixed resolved/unresolved rows, and a regression guard added after self-review (a corrupted row with `resolution_date` before `created_at` would otherwise silently pollute the mean with a negative latency). Standard-tier self-review, no regressions to `lessonsEmitted`/`distinctVentures`/`lessonsPerTraversal`. Handoffs LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 97.
- **GATE_SUBAGENT_EVIDENCE closed a fleet-wide fail-open — required sub-agent evidence is now actually enforced at every handoff** - PR #6141 (SD-FDBK-INFRA-FIX-GATE-SUBAGENT-001)
  - **What shipped**: self-sourced from a peer worker's RCA report, independently re-verified by reading the exact cited code at HEAD before creating the SD. `scripts/modules/handoff/gates/subagent-evidence-gate.js` computes `REQUIRED_SUBAGENTS[ctx.handoffType] || []` — but none of the 3 validation-context builders (`BaseExecutor.js`'s execute-path `validationContext`, `HandoffOrchestrator.js`'s precheck-path and `--evaluate` dry-run-path contexts) ever set `ctx.handoffType`, so the lookup always resolved to an empty array and the gate has trivially passed with `score:100` fleet-wide **since introduction**, regardless of whether any required sub-agent (TESTING, SECURITY, VALIDATION, Explore, RETRO) had actually run. CLAUDE.md's stated rule ("handoff blocks with SUBAGENT_EVIDENCE_MISSING if no fresh row exists") had never actually been enforced by this gate. Fixed by adding `handoffType: this.handoffType` / `handoffType: normalizedType` at all 3 sites, mirroring the value expression already used elsewhere in each file for the same purpose. `subagent-evidence-gate.js` itself and `required-subagents.js` were deliberately left unchanged — the bug was purely in the upstream callers never populating the field the gate already keyed on correctly.
  - **Independently confirmed 4 times before any code was written**: 2 LEAD-phase sub-agents (validation-agent, risk-agent) directly inspected the live code at HEAD before the PRD was written; risk-agent additionally measured the fleet blast radius (~53/55 currently-active SDs would newly hit `SUBAGENT_EVIDENCE_MISSING` the instant a raw fix reaches `main`, since they'd been relying — unknowingly — on the fail-open). That rollout-timing decision (setting the pre-existing `LEO_DISABLE_SUBAGENT_EVIDENCE_GATE=1` kill-switch, staged fleet broadcast) was explicitly flagged as a cross-worker coordination call and signaled to the active coordinator rather than decided unilaterally, while the code fix itself proceeded as an independently-scoped parallel track — this PR's own EXEC-TO-PLAN handoff is a live self-referential proof the fix works (`GATE_SUBAGENT_EVIDENCE` scored 100% with real TESTING+SECURITY evidence correctly detected, where it would previously have silently passed with zero evidence).
  - **Asymmetric, judgment-scoped test coverage**: the 2 `HandoffOrchestrator.js` sites got full behavioral regression tests via the codebase's existing proven mock-and-inspect-context harness. The `BaseExecutor.js` site — a ~700-line template method with 10+ dynamic-import dependencies (claim validity, claim-eligibility fencing, migration checks, gate-policy resolution, telemetry) standing between the method's entry and the one object literal being fixed — got a lightweight structural/source-text regression test instead of a ~10-mock integration harness, a tradeoff explicitly assessed and endorsed by 4 independent EXEC/VERIFICATION-phase sub-agents (TESTING, SECURITY, VALIDATION, REGRESSION) rather than assumed.
  - **A second, unrelated bug surfaced and RCA'd while shipping this one**: the LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL handoff was itself blocked by `GATE_MULTI_SESSION_CLAIM_CONFLICT` reporting a live peer session as the claim holder, even though `strategic_directives_v2.claiming_session_id` correctly named this session as owner. RCA traced it to a duplicated claim-ownership invariant across two tables (`strategic_directives_v2.claiming_session_id` vs `claude_sessions.sd_key`) with no reconciliation: the peer's OS process was confirmed dead, but a heartbeat-keepalive mechanism that ignores `is_alive` kept its stale `sd_key` stamp reading as "active" in `v_active_sessions`, and this gate reads that surface instead of the authoritative owner column (unlike the adjacent `claim-validity-gate.js`, which correctly reads the owner column and already passed). Unblocked surgically via the existing holder-pinned `releaseClaimBothSurfaces()` helper (clears only the dead peer's stale stamp; the SD-side clause is a guaranteed no-op since it isn't the true owner) — no files or other sessions' claims touched. Logged as a deferred harness-backlog item (4th witness of `PAT-LEO-INFRA-WRITER-CONSUMER-ASYMMETRY-001`) rather than fixed inline, since it's out of this SD's scope.
  - **Verification**: 26 new/modified regression tests across 3 files (`HandoffOrchestrator.dryrun-handofftype.test.js` new, `HandoffOrchestrator.precheck-policy.test.js` extended, `BaseExecutor.handofftype.test.js` new), plus the pre-existing `subagent-evidence-gate.test.js` (TS-1–TS-7, unmodified, already covers the gate's own logic exhaustively once fed a real `handoffType`). Full handoff-module regression sweep: 45 files / 463 tests, 0 regressions. Deep-tier `/ship` review (touches core protocol enforcement): multi-agent adversarial pass, zero findings. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN, PLAN-TO-EXEC, EXEC-TO-PLAN 95%, PLAN-TO-LEAD 97%, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL (precheck 99%).

- **Belt claim-eligibility now honors chairman_ratified + soft_depends_on, closing a prose-only encoding gap** - PR #6084 (SD-LEO-INFRA-BELT-CLAIM-ELIGIBILITY-001)
  - **What shipped**: sourced by Adam per the coordinator co-drive review (2026-07-13) — the shared dispatch-eligibility predicate (`lib/fleet/claim-eligibility.cjs`, used by both the worker self-claim path and the coordinator sweep path) didn't read two `metadata` fields Adam already stamps at sourcing time, so "is this SD claimable yet" lived only in prose/human relay. FR-1: added `chairmanRatificationPending`, a new `INELIGIBILITY_AXES` entry blocking dispatch only when `metadata.chairman_ratified === false` (fail-open on absence/true), also added to `CLAIM_WRITE_FENCE_AXES` alongside `needs_coordinator_review`. FR-2: folded `metadata.soft_depends_on` into the EXISTING `draftDepsSatisfied()` live-status dependency re-check — not a second predicate, per the SD's explicit scope constraint.
  - **A live-data check during LEAD-phase verification caught a real would-be regression before implementation was finalized**: the SD's abstract FR-2 spec described `soft_depends_on` as "any listed" SD keys (implying a clean structured list), but the one live example in the DB (`SD-LEO-INFRA-UNIVERSAL-LOOP-GOVERNANCE-001`) is free-form prose — `"D8 (SD-LEO-INFRA-OPERATOR-CONTRACT-GATE-001) provides merge-time enrollment; can build in parallel, integrate at PLAN"`. A naive whole-string match against `sd_key` would have treated the entire sentence as a literal, non-matching key and wrongly blocked that already-in-progress live SD the moment this change shipped. Fixed by adding `SD_KEY_TOKEN_RE` to extract the embedded `SD-XXX-YYY-NNN`-shaped token from the prose instead. Caught by checking the actual DB row against the regression pin ("no existing claimable SD becomes silently unclaimable"), not just unit-test fixtures.
  - **Verification**: 14 new/updated unit tests across 2 files (`claim-eligibility-chairman-ratified.test.js` new; `claim-eligibility.test.js` extended for the prose-extraction and array/string/fail-open cases), plus one exact-array `CLAIM_WRITE_FENCE_AXES` pin test updated for the new axis. Full claim-eligibility-related suite: 51 files, 580 tests, 0 regressions — confirmed independently by both the TESTING sub-agent (96% confidence, 497/497 tests) and a REGRESSION sub-agent (95% confidence, confirmed additive-only diff and unchanged exports/call-sites). Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN 94%, PLAN-TO-EXEC 96%, EXEC-TO-PLAN 94%, PLAN-TO-LEAD 92%, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 98%. Retrospective `aae0096b` (90/100 quality).

- **Central liveness stamper: GHA-cron resolver + per-script instrumentation closes the 108/134-row UNVERIFIED gap** - PRs #6059, #6063, #6067 (SD-FDBK-ENH-CENTRAL-LIVENESS-STAMPER-001)
  - **What shipped**: chairman-ratified (build-vs-run D-set, D4) — `periodic_process_registry` was 94% UNVERIFIED (108/134 rows) because most rows had no real liveness signal wired up. Widened `liveness_source`'s CHECK constraint to allow `'github_actions_api'` and added a `last_state_changed_at` anchor column (migration `20260713_periodic_process_registry_gha_source_and_state_anchor.sql`, applies out-of-band per this table's established convention). Added a GitHub Actions run resolver (`lib/periodic-liveness/gha-run-resolver.mjs`) that polls the real GH Actions runs API once per watcher cycle and stamps the 68 `gha_cron:*` rows from their latest scheduled run (a failed latest run classifies OVERDUE, not UNVERIFIED). Instrumented 29 distinct scripts (the 25 backing the 26 `standard_loop:*` rows — the coordinator has no single shared runner, each loop is independently armed — plus 4 `cron_script:*` rows confirmed to have a real GHA invoker) to self-stamp at end-of-tick via the existing `stampLastFired()` helper. Classified the 5 `cron_script:*` rows confirmed to have no invoker anywhere as `currently_expected_active=false`. Added persistent-UNVERIFIED escalation: a row continuously UNVERIFIED for over 7 days now escalates the same way an OVERDUE row does, anchored on the new column (only advances on a genuine state transition, never a same-cycle reaffirm).
  - **Two design gaps caught and fixed before any code was written**, by a pre-EXEC TESTING sub-agent check on the PRD: the existing `stampLastFired()` helper hard-scopes itself to `liveness_source='self_stamped'` rows by its own docstring — the plan to reuse it for the new `github_actions_api` source would have silently no-op'd (fixed by adding a sibling `stampFromGithubActionsRun()` instead of misusing it); and the ">7 days" escalation had no durable timestamp anchor to measure against, since the existing `last_state` column is overwritten every watcher cycle regardless of transition (fixed via the new `last_state_changed_at` column).
  - **One real bug caught after merge, by a post-EXEC TESTING sub-agent check during EXEC-TO-PLAN**: the merged code bundled the new anchor column's write into the SAME `.update()` statement as the pre-existing `last_state` write. Since the migration adding that column applies out-of-band and this repo allows code to merge ahead of its own migration, that bundled write would fail the WHOLE statement atomically in the merge-to-migration window, silently breaking `last_state`'s own advancement too — reproducing a failure class the same file already had a documented guard against for a sibling column (`consecutive_miss_count`, from a prior SD). Fixed by decoupling into an independently fail-soft `stampStateChangeAnchor()`, matching that existing precedent, shipped as a follow-up (PR #6067, 3 new regression tests). CI's `schema-reference-lint` independently caught the same forward-reference on the next push, resolved with a `schema-lint-disable-line` annotation matching the sibling column's own existing precedent.
  - **PR-size note**: the 28-script instrumentation pass was split into its own PR (#6063) from the FR-1/FR-2/FR-5 core (#6059) specifically to keep two interdependent-but-separable units independently reviewable; #6063 was originally stacked on #6059's branch but GitHub auto-closed it when that branch was deleted post-merge (commits unaffected) — re-opened directly against `main`.
  - **Verification**: 117 new/modified unit tests (GHA-resolver pure mapping, the `stampFromGithubActionsRun` sibling function, `evaluateRow`'s new branch, `hasCrossedUnverifiedThreshold`'s per-episode dedup, both backfill scripts, `stampStateChangeAnchor`'s fail-soft behavior) plus a static wiring test asserting all 29 instrumented scripts reference their correct `process_key`. Full `periodic-liveness`/`coordinator`/`scripts`/`cron`/`sweep`/`governance` regression sweep: 1877 tests pass, 0 regressions. `node --check` on all 33 touched files. `schema-reference-lint --diff` 0 violations. TESTING sub-agent CONDITIONAL_PASS 93% (migration application itself is a tracked out-of-band deployment follow-up), SECURITY sub-agent PASS 93%. Handoffs LEAD-TO-PLAN, PLAN-TO-EXEC, EXEC-TO-PLAN 90%, PLAN-TO-LEAD 95%, LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 96%. Retrospective `6af1f048` (90/100).

- **L7: vision_key now stamped at SD creation, closing the vision-fidelity gate's 100% no_vision_key skip** - PR #6083 (SD-LEO-INFRA-VISION-KEY-STAMP-AT-SD-CREATION-001)
  - **What shipped**: chairman-ratified (Vision Loop-Completeness Map @ f2b64a94, loop L7) — the `VISION_FIDELITY_GATE` (PLAN-TO-LEAD) had never executed a single real evaluation: 2142/2142 prior evaluations short-circuited with `skipped_reason=no_vision_key`, because no SD-creation path ever stamped `sd.metadata.vision_key`. `lib/sd-creation/pipeline.js`'s `createSD()` — the single shared insert convergence point for every creation lane (direct-args, `--from-proposal`, `--child`, `--from-plan`, `--from-feedback`, UAT, learn) — now gap-fill stamps `metadata.vision_key` to the canonical, chairman-approved `VISION-EHG-L1-001` whenever it's absent, mirroring the existing `min_tier_rank` gap-fill pattern already in the same function. An already-present value (a validated `--vision-key`, or an inherited child value) is never overwritten.

Without this fix, stamping `vision_key` alone would have just changed the skip reason from `no_vision_key` to a silent "vision_key not found — advisory pass," never producing a real verdict.   - **Verification**: 6 new unit tests for the gap-fill predicate (mirrors the established `min_tier_rank` FR-3 test convention) + 3 new real-DB integration tests (`tests/integration/vision-key-stamp-gate-evaluates.test.js`) proving `executeVisionFidelity()` reaches a genuine PASS/FAIL/WARNING verdict for a vision_key-carrying SD (via an injected LLM stub, zero cost) while confirming the un-stamped-legacy-SD skip baseline is unchanged.
