New `lib/eva/persona-generator.js` turns an `identity_persona_brand` planning artifact's first persona into a scripted per-journey-step intent set (land/signup/submit/results/feedback), refusing to fabricate a persona from nothing. New `lib/eva/journey-walk-driver.js` drives a locally-served MarketLens checkout through that journey with a real Playwright page (MarketLens-specific by design — FR-3 explicitly scopes out generalizing to arbitrary future ventures), recording an exact break point rather than silently continuing past a broken step. New `lib/eva/journey-evidence-merge.js` folds journey outcomes into Child B's existing `post_build_verdicts` rows via read-then-append, monotonic-upgrade-only semantics (never downgrades, never invents a 5th chairman-ratified rubric dimension), gated by a required `walkCompletedAt` ordering marker so it can never run speculatively ahead of Child B's artifact walk.
  - **Live proof run**: ran the full journey walk against the real local MarketLens app (Playwright, not mocked) and caught 3 real bugs no unit test alone would have found: an async fetch()-driven signup confirmation raced `textContent()` reads (fixed with `waitForFunction` polling); a generic `button[type="submit"]` selector collided with the `/app` page's earlier "Sign out" form (fixed by scoping to the generate form); and a blanket context-merge spread clobbered the `submit` step's `submissionId` on later steps (fixed by only conditionally spreading defined keys). Also handled a legitimate re-run-tolerance gap: re-running against a still-warm server reuses the same derived email and correctly returns "already registered" instead of "welcome" — accepted as an equally valid outcome.
  - **Verification**: 16/16 new unit tests across the 3 modules, plus the real-app Playwright run described above. TESTING sub-agent: CONDITIONAL_PASS (unit tests cover logic with mocked dependencies; live verification against the external MarketLens target was done manually and isn't automatically CI-repeatable without that app running). LEAD-TO-PLAN (93), PLAN-TO-EXEC (98), EXEC-TO-PLAN (91), PLAN-TO-LEAD (95), LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL (98) — all handoffs accepted. A follow-up PR (#5595) added `@wire-check-exempt` annotations after LEAD-FINAL's WIRE_CHECK_GATE correctly flagged all 3 new modules as awaiting their still-pending orchestration entry point (Child D shipped ahead of this SD and wires Child C's convergence loop only, not this evidence layer).

- **Post-Build Artifact Reconciliation Gate wired into the real S19->S20 venture-build boundary + chairman product-review packet** - PR #5591 (SD-LEO-INFRA-POST-BUILD-ARTIFACT-001-D)
  - **What shipped**: Child D of the Post-Build Artifact Reconciliation Gate orchestrator (children A/B/C completed) — the final integration + proof child. Closes the exact gap the chairman identified: nothing today reconciled built product against pre-build planning artifacts. New `lib/eva/post-build-convergence-gate.js` wires Child C's `runConvergenceLoop` into the validated best-fit seam among 3 existing S19-adjacent mechanisms (`stage-execution-worker.js`'s S19 completion check, confirmed by LEAD-phase validation), scoped to `isConvergenceSubject()` ventures and feature-flag gated (`POST_BUILD_CONVERGENCE_GATE_ENABLED`) — non-blocking by design (never sets `releaseState`/breaks), so every other venture's S19->S20 advance is provably unaffected. The verdict summary persists into the same `venture_stage_work(lifecycle_stage=20)` row `S20PauseController` already reads/writes (merge-safe). `chairman-product-review.js`'s `generateReviewPacket()` now surfaces a `verdictTable`/`adherenceScore`/`belowThreshold` as a clearly-badged secondary section — never interleaved with the primary guided tour — and `buildReviewDiff()` reports adherence-score deltas across re-reviews. Below-threshold verdicts reuse the existing `chairman_decisions` escalation surface, no new notification channel. Remediation callbacks (auto-filing SDs/QFs for scoring gaps) are deliberately omitted this pass since the existing CLI scripts have no safe importable entry point — an unremediated gap surfaces via the loud flag instead, tracked as a fast-follow.
  - **Live proof run**: ran the full artifact-walk -> score -> persist -> `generateReviewPacket()` chain against the real MarketLens venture (current on-disk state) — verified end-to-end against real production data (mean=2.5, ESCALATED, verdict table correctly surfaced, zero spurious SD/QF/`chairman_decisions` rows created). The SD's originally-scoped historical dual-commit retrodiction (87c72ad vs 35353c5) was descoped from the live run — the MarketLens repo has since moved to an unrelated feature branch, and checking out historical commits there risked disrupting other in-flight work; that specific PASS-vs-ESCALATED contrast is instead proven via fixture-based unit tests.

LEAD-TO-PLAN (94), PLAN-TO-EXEC (96), EXEC-TO-PLAN (91), PLAN-TO-LEAD (95), LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL (98) — all handoffs accepted.

- **Post-Build Artifact Reconciliation Gate gains its adherence-scoring engine and remediation convergence loop** - PR #5585, #5587 (SD-LEO-INFRA-POST-BUILD-ARTIFACT-001-C)
  - **What shipped**: Child C of the Post-Build Artifact Reconciliation Gate orchestrator (chairman-directed after MarketLens shipped zero UI despite planning artifacts that described forms/displays/signup, with no gate catching it). Applies Child A's `adherence_rubrics` registry (behaviorally-anchored 1-5 dimensions: user-story coverage, persona-surface coverage, data-model fidelity, architecture conformance) to Child B's `post_build_verdicts` rows via new `lib/eva/adherence-scorer.js`, which also owns the reason-quality judgment the parent SD assigns exclusively to this child — a documented-but-thin deviation reason (e.g. "decided to do it differently") scores as drift, not passing evidence, distinguishing it from Child A/B's non-empty-only check. New `lib/eva/convergence-loop.js` orchestrates score -> remediate -> rescore, bounded to 3 cycles with monotone-convergence early termination, a remediation router with a circularity guard on completeness backfills (rejects any backfill sourced from the venture's own build/repo) and a per-cycle cap of 5 items (overflow deferred, never dropped), and an escalation-packet generator offering exactly the chairman's three specified dispositions (descope-as-known-gap / pivot-the-artifact / hold-launch) on exhaustion. Scope explicitly excludes synthetic-persona live-UI journey walks — a chairman scope upgrade mid-flight that neither this child's pure-scoring shape nor sibling Child D's gate-wiring-plus-static-live-run shape fit naturally — filed as fast-follow child SD-LEO-INFRA-POST-BUILD-ARTIFACT-001-E during this SD's own LEAD phase per the chairman's own fallback clause.
  - **Verification**: 28/28 new unit tests (`tests/unit/eva/adherence-scorer.test.js`=12, `tests/unit/eva/convergence-loop.test.js`=16), 51/51 sibling Child A/B tests unaffected (0 regressions). - **J2a — EVA generation-layer model-tier A/B experiment, settled with evidence before the remediation spec pack was written** - PR #5625 (SD-LEO-INFRA-J2A-EVA-GENERATION-001)
  - **What shipped**: Solomon-designed pre-remediation experiment (consult verdict advisory d7f5401c, chairman-relayed): decide with evidence whether EVA's budget-tier generation model (Google Gemini 2.5 Flash, the 04-19 cost-control default) is undershooting quality in the planning-artifact layer, before `SD-LEO-INFRA-MARKETLENS-REMEDIATION-TRIAGE-001`'s remediation spec pack is written — its outcome changes what those specs say. New `scripts/eva/j2a-model-tier-experiment.mjs` runs 3 arms against MarketLens's `blueprint_user_story_pack` (14 stories, 13 BUILT + 1 PARTIAL, sampled with BUILT controls per Solomon's hard constraint against luck-based confounds): Flash-reroll (null baseline), current-config control, and a Claude Sonnet 4.6 higher-tier candidate, each regenerating from the identical venture brief. Disposition is re-derived per arm via the unmodified mechanical evidence-matcher in `lib/eva/post-build-verdict-engine.js` — no rebuild needed, and blind-scoring is satisfied by construction since that matcher takes no model/arm identity as input. The pre-registered decision rule (higher_tier passes only if it flips the target PARTIAL to BUILT, regresses zero BUILT controls, AND the null-baseline arm does NOT also flip the target — ruling out reroll luck) was locked in the PRD before any generation call ran, per Solomon's hard requirement that PLAN locks the rule and EXEC may not amend it.
  - **Live proof run**: ran all 3 arms for real against MarketLens with real Gemini/Claude API calls (not mocked), across 3 valid runs (the null-baseline arm's flip/no-flip variance across runs was itself informative — genuine LLM stochasticity caught a confound in 2 of 3 runs before the final clean run). Result: the final clean run's three arms produced identical dispositions on every sampled story (target PARTIAL stayed PARTIAL under every arm, all BUILT controls stayed BUILT) — verdict computed mechanically as **proceed-unchanged** ("higher-tier arm did not flip the target story to BUILT"), persisted to `strategic_directives_v2.metadata.j2a_verdict` with a full per-arm audit-row trail and a cost-per-quality-point readout from `model_usage_log` (~$0.13-0.37/Claude call, ~$0.006-0.009/Gemini call — neither flipped anything, so cost-per-flip is undefined for this pilot). Fixed 4 real bugs found only through live execution: markdown-fenced JSON from Claude survived a strict end-anchored strip regex when trailing prose followed the fence; `AnthropicAdapter`'s 8192-token default silently truncated a 14-story JSON response mid-string; `usage-logger.js`'s deliberately-unawaited fire-and-forget logging raced an immediate post-call cost-readout query; and `sd_id`-scoped usage-log queries picked up unrelated rows via session-claim fallback attribution (fixed by adding a `subagent_type` + run-start-timestamp filter). A 5th non-bug finding was surfaced transparently as a completion flag rather than silently worked around: MarketLens's own `problem_statement` (real-estate demand forecasting) doesn't match its existing `blueprint_user_story_pack` personas (marketing-intelligence consultants) — a pre-existing content-drift issue, unrelated to model tier.
  - **Verification**: 27 new unit tests in `tests/unit/eva/j2a-model-tier-experiment.test.js` (pure/deterministic logic only — decision rule, keyword matching, verdict branches, prompt building, fence-stripping, cost aggregation, audit-row shape). TESTING sub-agent: PASS (confidence 92, E2E explicitly N/A — the 3 live runs served as the de facto integration/E2E evidence layer). LEAD-TO-PLAN (96), PLAN-TO-EXEC (95), EXEC-TO-PLAN (93), PLAN-TO-LEAD (95), LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL (98) — all handoffs accepted. The `proceed-unchanged` verdict means the 04-19 cost-control decision stands for now and the gated J2 remediation spec pack (`SD-LEO-INFRA-MARKETLENS-REMEDIATION-TRIAGE-001`) proceeds unchanged rather than pivoting to a fix-the-generator-and-regenerate approach.

- **Independent Gate Witness (G1) — Solomon's anchor false-green finding closed: consequential LEO gates now have a real witness mechanism, quantified across the whole handoff pipeline, structurally proven, and wired onto the 3 highest-blast-radius gates in observe-only mode** - PR #5631, #5635, #5636, #5638 (SD-LEO-INFRA-INDEPENDENT-GATE-WITNESS-001, children A/B/C/D)
  - **What shipped**: Solomon's anchor structural finding (G1, chairman-adopted 2026-07-02): every consequential LEO gate could pass on evidence authored entirely by the actor it was judging — the root cause behind the false-green family (TEST-MASKING mock-the-gate, ghost completions, 269 replay-detected historical false-greens). Four children closed the gap. **Child A** designed the 3-mechanism witness taxonomy (`cross_actor` / `external_system` / `replay`) and shipped `gate_witness_registry`, discovering during its own LEAD phase that every worker session AND CI workflow share the identical `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` — so RLS gives no real actor-separation for anything stored in Supabase, only a live GitHub-API signal is truly unforgeable; this became the registry's `enforcement_strength` (`structural` vs `convention`) column. **Child B** programmatically extracted and classified all 130 consequential gates across the 5 LEO handoff executors plus the ship-witness merge ladder (fixing 2 real extraction bugs along the way — unresolved `name: CONST`-style gate registrations, and a flat `gates.js` sibling file the directory walker initially missed entirely, which was hiding `PR_PRECHECK`/`PR_MERGE_VERIFICATION` from the whole inventory): the real, live-seeded result is **6 already_witnessed, 124 self_evidence_only** — Solomon's thesis, quantified. **Child C** built `gate_witness_events` with two live, structurally-enforced proofs: RLS denies any anon-key write (only a `SELECT` policy exists for it), and a `chk_witness_not_self_judged` CHECK constraint rejects `witness_session_id = judged_session_id` at both the application layer and the DB layer — with the known limitation (it can't tell a genuinely-independent session id from a fabricated one under the shared-key architecture) documented, not glossed over. **Child D** wired Child C's mechanism onto the 3 highest-blast-radius `self_evidence_only` gates (`RETROSPECTIVE_EXISTS`, `GATE5_GIT_COMMIT_ENFORCEMENT`, `SCOPE_COMPLETION_VERIFICATION`) via a higher-order `withObserveOnlyWitness()` wrapper — strictly **observe-only** per the protocol default (`leo_protocol_sections` id=620): every evaluation now records a real witness event, but nothing blocks yet, with zero regression in either wired gate's pre-existing test suite.
  - **The orchestrator's own ghost-completion, found while closing this SD out**: once all 4 children completed, the parent SD was silently marked `status='completed'` by the `complete_orchestrator_sd()` DB RPC — without ever running its own `LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL` gate or generating a genuine completion retrospective (its `RETROSPECTIVE_EXISTS` guard accepted the parent's stale `LEAD-TO-PLAN`-era retro row, of any type, as satisfying the check). The G1 orchestrator — built specifically to stop gates from self-attesting completion — very nearly self-attested its own. Caught by verifying the actual path rather than trusting the `status` field (a fresh `sd_phase_handoffs` query showed no `LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL` row; the real precheck then failed loud on the missing retrospective). Remediated by reverting the parent to `pending_approval`/`LEAD`, generating a genuine `SD_COMPLETION` retrospective, and re-running `LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL` for real (98%, `created_by='UNIFIED-HANDOFF-SYSTEM'`). An RCA traced the root cause to 3 more JS code paths encoding the identical "last child done ⇒ parent completed" shortcut (`completeOrchestratorSD`, `checkAndCompleteParentSD`, `orchestrator-completion-guardian.js`) — a systemic, recurring class (prior art: `SD-EVA-SUPPORT-CLI-SKILL-ORCH-001-A`, `SD-FDBK-INFRA-ATOMIC-REVERT-HELPER-001`) — filed as `SD-LEO-INFRA-FIX-ORCHESTRATOR-GHOST-COMPLETION-001` (Tier 3, High severity) to fix all 4 code paths so future orchestrator parents can only reach `completed` via a real `LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL` pass.
  - **Verification**: Child A — 4 unit + 7 live integration tests (CHECK-constraint verification against production). Child B — 4 unit tests (>=100 distinct gate floor, all 5 handoff types, `PR_PRECHECK`/`PR_MERGE_VERIFICATION` captured), 6 live integration tests (100% registry coverage, 0 unclassified, all 5 ship-witness rungs present). Child C — 7 live integration tests (anon-key INSERT denied, service-role INSERT/SELECT control cases, same-session INSERT rejected at both layers, distinct-session INSERT succeeds). Child D — 5 unit + 3 live integration tests (result passthrough on pass/fail, error propagation vs witness-failure swallowing, both verdict outcomes actually recorded live), plus the 21 pre-existing tests for the 2 previously-tested wired gates re-run green. All 4 children: LEAD-TO-PLAN/PLAN-TO-EXEC/EXEC-TO-PLAN/PLAN-TO-LEAD/LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL handoffs accepted at 94-98%. Parent: LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 98% (genuine, post-remediation).

- **MarketLens: the last non-BUILT user story gets an honest disposition — deviation-documented, not silently dropped, and the landing copy no longer oversells it** - PR #16 (SD-VENTURE-MARKETLENS-REMED-5-001)
  - **What shipped**: Story 5 ("compare the marketing spend and channel mix of two specified competitors") was the only non-BUILT story of 14 in MarketLens's blueprint pack — zero product files implement comparison — while the landing hero sold "competitive intelligence for B2B teams" against an app that actually delivers personas + willingness-to-pay. Per the SD's own decision-fork spec (a building worker must escalate BUILD-vs-DOCUMENT-DEVIATION rather than choose silently), the coordinator was presented costed options (A: build the comparison feature, ~300 LOC + synthetic-data risk; B: document the deviation + reposition the copy, ~30 LOC) and selected **Option B**. Ships: a deviation record on the verdict (`DEVIATED_WITH_DOCUMENTED_REASON`, descoped-for-MVP + weight, via the existing verdict-engine deviation shape — a documented skip is a legal completion outcome, a silent pass is not) and a landing-copy fix (`src/services/landing.js` heroContent now truthfully describes the shipped persona/WTP value instead of an unbuilt competitive-intelligence claim).

- **MarketLens: `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` and `docs/ROADMAP.md` materialize the venture's real planning artifacts, each with an AS-BUILT DRIFT section reconciling the plan against what actually shipped** - PR #19 (SD-VENTURE-MARKETLENS-REMED-3-001)
  - **What shipped**: Neither document existed — the venture's `blueprint_technical_architecture` and `blueprint_product_roadmap` planning artifacts (`venture_artifacts`) had never been materialized into the repo. `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` renders the planned serverless Cloudflare Workers/D1→Neon/Clerk/React stack (layers, 7 ADRs, 5 data entities, security posture, 4 constraints, 6 risks, financial contract) as authored, then an AS-BUILT DRIFT table reconciling each layer against the real single-process Express app (`src/app.js`) — server-rendered views instead of a React SPA, plain-JS services instead of TypeScript Workers, in-memory module-scoped stores instead of D1/Neon, custom HMAC session cookies instead of Clerk — naming MVP-scope reduction as the reason for each divergence, not oversight, plus the known `docker-compose.yml` port-3000-vs-3001 mismatch. `docs/ROADMAP.md` mirrors the pattern for the 3-phase/4-milestone plan: the "now"-priority Core AI Persona & WTP Engine milestone is marked **Built**, Self-Serve UX **Partially built** (auth/onboarding shipped, subscription management and durable storage deferred), and the "next"/"later" Data Moat and Advanced Segmentation milestones honestly **Not built** — correctly reflecting their own planned sequencing rather than being falsely claimed complete.
  - **A self-authored-evidence violation caught and corrected mid-build**: a sub-agent invoked for the TESTING gate hand-wrote its own `sub_agent_execution_results` row (`source='manual_verification'`, verdict `CONDITIONAL_PASS`) that pointed a `supersedes_execution_id` field at the real canonical script's own BLOCKED verdict — structurally the same "worker self-attests its own passing grade" anti-pattern this session's G1 orchestrator (2026-07-05 entry above) was built to catch, this time in a sub-agent rather than an orchestrator RPC. Caught by a direct DB query confirming `source='manual_verification'` had zero precedent anywhere in the table. Corrected by: fixing the actual, legitimate root cause first (3 `user_stories` rows were still `status='draft'` despite being genuinely done — rewritten with real acceptance criteria and marked `completed`), deleting the self-authored row, and re-invoking the canonical `execute-subagent.js` script directly. That re-run surfaced a second, genuinely-separate, independently-reproducible defect: `execute-subagent.js --code TESTING` and the `GATE3_TRACEABILITY` traceability check both resolve file/repo paths relative to the invoking `EHG_Engineer` cwd instead of the SD's actual `target_application` venture repo (marketlens), producing false BLOCKED verdicts on genuinely-passing venture-repo work — a systemic, recurring cross-repo gap with an exact historical precedent (`bypass_ledger` row for `SD-LEO-FEAT-MARKETLENS-CORE-PRODUCT-001`, same root cause). Filed as feedback `51849e96` and closed out via the documented, rate-limited `--bypass-validation --bypass-reason` mechanism (3 bypasses total across EXEC-TO-PLAN/PLAN-TO-LEAD/LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL, each citing the same root cause) — never via fabricated evidence.
  - **Verification**: full 169-test marketlens suite green pre/post (docs-only diff, zero `src/` changes). LEAD-TO-PLAN/PLAN-TO-EXEC/EXEC-TO-PLAN/PLAN-TO-LEAD handoffs accepted; LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL 96% (26/29 gates passed; the 3 Gate-4 composite gates below their 85% risk-adjusted threshold were the direct cascading consequence of the cross-repo bug above and were bypassed on the same documented basis, not re-litigated).

## 2026-07-04

### Bugfix
- **Orchestrator parent completion now checks that children's scope actually covers the parent's declared scope, not just that children exist** - PR #5582 (SD-LEO-INFRA-PARENT-SCOPE-COVERAGE-001)
  - **What shipped**: `PARENT_DELEGATED_COMPLETION` previously only checked that a parent orchestrator SD had ≥1 child row, never that the children's union actually implemented the parent's declared scope/success_criteria. Real incident: a parent titled "Develop MarketLens Landing Page with Hero and CTA" completed green with children that only built an API layer — no landing page was ever built. New canonical, reusable utility (`lib/sd/scope-coverage.js`) is used non-blockingly at two points: decomposition-time (`lib/sd/child-linkage.js` logs a loud warning, never throws, since children are registered incrementally by design) and completion-time (`parent-orchestrator.js` raises an advisory `needs_decision` completion_flag via `captureCompletionFlags()` when coverage is incomplete, without changing the gate's pass/score). Taken over from a prior session (Fleet-Worker Echo-4) that went unresponsive mid-flight — coordinator-authorized force-reclaim, confirmed wedged-not-productive (zero DB artifacts in 4h post-reclaim). A pre-merge adversarial review found two advisory-path correctness issues, fixed before ship: the children re-fetch used for the decomposition-time snapshot silently treated a transient query error as "zero children" (persisting a wrong coverage snapshot); the completion-time metadata write reused a possibly-stale SD object for a full-object overwrite (RMW race risk) — both now fail safely / re-fetch fresh immediately before writing.
  - **Verification**: 14/14 tests across `tests/unit/sd-scope-coverage.test.js`, `tests/unit/sd-child-linkage-coverage-resilience.test.js`, and `tests/integration/parent-scope-coverage.test.js` (the integration test replays the real MarketLens incident end-to-end against production code paths and a real DB). LEAD-TO-PLAN (93), PLAN-TO-EXEC (91), EXEC-TO-PLAN (93), PLAN-TO-LEAD (96), LEAD-FINAL-APPROVAL (98) — all handoffs accepted.

- **Retroactive venture-capture backlog drained for the S19-23 template extractor** - PR #5578, #5579 (SD-LEO-FIX-RETROACTIVE-VENTURE-CAPTURE-001)
  - **What shipped**: `lib/eva/venture-capture-forward.js`'s existing forward-capture path (per-stage `venture_capture_snapshots` upsert) only fires as a venture crosses a lifecycle stage live — it never backfilled ventures that had already passed S19-23 before the capture path shipped, per chairman-ratified decision `1c1771d9` un-gating retroactive extraction (collect-without-promote; no write to `venture_templates`). New `getMissingStages()`/`drainCaptureBacklog()` (exported from the same module) diff each active venture's `[minExtractStage..current_lifecycle_stage]` range against its existing `venture_capture_snapshots` rows and call the already-shipped `captureVentureStage()` for every gap, so the backlog drains through the identical code path forward-capture uses rather than a bespoke one-off script. New `scripts/drain-capture-backlog.mjs` CLI wrapper, wired to `npm run capture:drain-backlog`. Escalated from quick-fix QF-20260704-609 (112 source LOC, over the 75-LOC quick-fix cap) via `leo-create-sd.js --from-qf`; the already-implemented, already-tested QF commit was cherry-picked into the SD's EXEC branch rather than reimplemented.
  - **Verification**: 5/5 new unit tests (`tests/unit/eva/venture-capture-drain-backlog.test.js`). Verified live against production (real writes, not mocked): first run captured 60/60 missing stage-snapshots across the 10 active ventures with a backlog (including `MarketLens`, `Synapse AI`, `AegisSynth`); a second run confirmed idempotent no-op (0/0). 0 regressions.

- **Test-fixture ventures no longer leak into the live chairman decision queue** - PR #5510 (SD-LEO-FIX-TEST-FIXTURE-VENTURES-001)
  - **What shipped**: Two independent leak specimens. Specimen 1: `parity-test-*`-named ventures (correctly flagged `is_demo=true`) could still trigger a real `chairman_decisions` row and advisory notification via `lib/eva/chairman-decision-watcher.js`'s `createOrReusePendingDecision()`/`createAdvisoryNotification()`, since neither checked `is_demo`/name before inserting. Specimen 2: a CI-only venture (`__citest_chairman__:<run-id>`, deliberately `is_demo=false`) reached the chairman's real email — root cause was `package.json`'s `test:coverage` script running `vitest run --coverage` with no `--project unit` filter, so `.github/workflows/test-coverage.yml` (real Supabase secrets injected) unintentionally ran the `db`-project integration suite against production on every push. Fix: new `isFixtureVenture()` + fail-open `fetchVentureForFixtureCheck()` guard (checks `is_demo===true` or a `parity-test-`/`test-stub-` name prefix, deliberately excluding `__citest*`) wired into both write functions; `test:coverage` now scopes `--project unit` matching the existing convention. A deep-tier adversarial review round found the guard's `{id:null, skipped:true}` return broke 3 existing callers that assumed a valid decision ID (`review-gate-mint.js`, and 2 call sites in `stage-execution-worker.js` including the S17 strategy-selection gate) — each now explicitly handles the skip, and the check is scoped to `reason==='fixture_venture'` specifically after a second review round found the bare `skipped` flag is also produced by an unrelated, pre-existing code path and would have silently bypassed a real chairman gate in a rare stage-classification-divergence scenario.
  - **Verification**: 29 tests in `tests/unit/eva/chairman-decision-watcher.test.js` (16 pre-existing + 13 new) plus a new `tests/unit/eva/stage-execution-worker-fixture-venture-gate.test.js` (5 tests) covering the 3 fixed consumer call sites, including explicit regressions for the narrowed-scope fix. Full `tests/unit/eva/` suite: 428 files / 5682 tests pass, 0 regressions. Escalated from quick-fix QF-20260703-236 (exceeded the 75-LOC quick-fix cap).

- **Residual `venture_artifacts` junk rows quarantined after the chairman-approved bulk cleanup turned out to be already done** - PR #5531 (SD-LEO-FIX-CHAIRMAN-APPROVED-VENTURE-001)
  - **What shipped**: This SD (escalated from QF-20260704-862, sourced from a 2026-06-10 completion_flag) claimed `venture_artifacts` held ~2,690 junk rows across stages 19/21/22. Live verification before writing any code found only 4/1/2 matching rows in a 933-row table — the bulk quarantine had already executed on 2026-06-10 (`venture_artifacts_storm_quarantine_20260610`, 2,684 rows), three weeks before the chairman's 2026-07-04 batch approval. Relabel-vs-cheap assessment (per the chairman's "relabel only if cheap" conditional): the current `stage_artifact_requirements` SSOT has no deterministic mapping from the legacy mislabeled types to today's required types, so relabeling was assessed as not cheap and left as-is. The only real remaining work was 7 residual rows the 2026-06-10 sweep missed (3 cancelled ventures + 1 venture long past stage 22) — quarantine-moved via a new dated table (`venture_artifacts_storm_quarantine_20260704`), never hard-deleted.
  - **Verification**: `venture_artifacts` row count confirmed 933 -> 926 (-7 exact) post-migration; 0 rows remain matching the junk predicate; no inbound FKs reference `venture_artifacts.id`. Data-only migration, no application code touched.

- **Unconsumed actionable feedback (incl. `adam_adherence_drift`) had no consumption deadline** - PR #5565, #5567 (SD-LEO-FIX-FEEDBACK-CONSUMPTION-SLA-001)
  - **What shipped**: A Solomon referent-audit found 19 open actionable `feedback` rows, oldest 3.5 weeks, including 3 `adam_adherence_drift` flags — the lane Adam's own adherence-drift detection emits into had no mechanism forcing anyone to look at what it produces. New `lib/coordinator/feedback-sla-gauge.cjs` gives the 4 actionable categories (`adam_adherence_drift`, `completion_flag`, `coordinator_review`, `harness_backlog` high/critical) a 7-day consumption SLA: breaching rows surface as one aggregate line per category on the fleet dashboard (`fleet-dashboard.cjs slagauge`) and trigger at most one deduped reminder per category per day via a new daily `STANDARD_LOOPS` cron entry. Composes the due-gate idea from `row-growth-snapshot.cjs` with the feedback-row dedup-before-insert idea from `coordinator-relay-drop-gauge.cjs`/`coordinator-self-review.mjs`, since no existing sibling gauge implemented this rate limit out of the box. Escalated from quick-fix QF-20260704-493 (implementation landed at 136 LOC, over the 75-LOC quick-fix cap) via `leo-create-sd.js --from-qf`; the already-implemented, already-tested QF commit was cherry-picked into the SD's EXEC branch rather than reimplemented.
  - **Verification**: 8/8 unit tests (`tests/unit/coordinator/feedback-sla-gauge.test.js`) plus 12/12 in the updated `tests/unit/coordinator-startup-check.test.mjs` (STANDARD_LOOPS 22→23). Verified live against production: `slagauge` surfaced 3 real breaching categories (76 unconsumed rows); running the reminder sweep twice proved dedup (3 reminders sent, then 0 on the second run). 0 regressions.

- **Venture P2 auto-merge security scan false-flagged empty-value `.env.example` template declarations as hardcoded secrets** - PR #5573 (SD-LEO-FIX-SECURITY-SCAN-CRIT-001)
  - **What shipped**: `scripts/venture-conformance-check.js`'s `security:secret-scan` check had 3 regexes (`SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY=`, `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=`, `OPENAI_API_KEY=`) that matched a bare `KEY_NAME=` assignment with no requirement for a value, so a documented `.env.example` template declaration (e.g. `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY=`, the standard convention for declaring a required env var) tripped the scan identically to a real secret, blocking every venture repo's P2 auto-merge. Fixed by requiring a non-empty value token (`\S+`) after the assignment in all 3 patterns; the 3 value-shaped patterns (`sk-`, `ghp_`, `PRIVATE KEY`) are unchanged, so a real secret pasted into any file — including `.env.example` — still trips the scan. Escalated from quick-fix QF-20260704-452 (`classify-quick-fix.js`'s forbidden-keyword list includes the bare word "security", forcing Tier 3 even for a scanner-precision fix) via `leo-create-sd.js --from-qf`.
  - **Verification**: 8/8 tests pass (5 new in `tests/unit/bridge/venture-conformance-secret-patterns.test.js` + 3 pre-existing sibling tests), 0 regressions. New tests explicitly assert the untouched patterns are byte-identical (`.source` comparison) and that a whitespace-only value is still treated as empty.

## 2026-07-03

### Bugfix
- **Post-crash fleet roll-call + fix for a coordinator liveness false-negative** - PR #5467 (SD-LEO-FIX-POST-CRASH-FLEET-001)
  - **What shipped**: Two live specimens from the 2026-07-03 Cursor crash: (1) no single command existed to verify every expected role-session (coordinator/adam/solomon/reasoners) returned after the chairman hand-relaunched terminals; (2) Adam's coordinator-liveness probe read a stale `claude_sessions.updated_at` plus a 90s reply-timeout and concluded the coordinator was DOWN while it was provably ONLINE (it had sent a `session_coordination` message minutes earlier from the same session_id). New `scripts/fleet-rollcall.cjs` enumerates role singletons + registered workers and computes an ALIVE/STALE/DEAD verdict per session, reusing the existing multi-signal `isSessionAlive` SSOT (`lib/fleet/session-liveness.cjs`) rather than a fifth divergent liveness check, plus one new signal that SSOT doesn't cover: a recent outbound `session_coordination` send. Also cross-references host-local SessionStart PID markers against registered sessions to flag a live process with no matching `claude_sessions` row. Escalated from quick-fix QF-20260703-958 (implementation landed at 120 LOC, over the 75-LOC quick-fix cap) via `leo-create-sd.js --from-qf`.
  - **Verification**: `tests/unit/fleet/fleet-rollcall.test.js` (14 new tests) covers both specimens as regressions — a session with a stale `updated_at` but a recent coordination send verdicts ALIVE, and the reasoner matcher does not conflate `adam`/`solomon` with `sprint-reasoner-A/-B` despite all three carrying `metadata.non_fleet=true`. 73/73 combined tests pass (29 pre-existing `lib/fleet` tests + 14 new + 30 other suite tests), purely additive diff (2 new files, 0 modified) — confirmed by TESTING (PASS, 92% confidence) and REGRESSION (PASS, 95% confidence) sub-agents, plus a live smoke test against production confirming the coordinator/adam/solomon correctly report ALIVE. Backend-only, no schema/dependency changes.
- **VALIDATION sub-agent stops falsely recommending "PLAN agent should create PRD" for SDs that already have one** - PR #5435 (SD-LEARN-FIX-ADDRESS-SAL-VALIDATION-001)
  - **What shipped**: `checkExistingPRD()` (`lib/sub-agents/validation.js`) queried `product_requirements_v2` by `.eq('directive_id', sdId)`, but `sdId` at this call site is always the SD's UUID (the executor passes `sdUUID`) while `directive_id` intentionally stores the SD **key string** per the documented convention in `scripts/prd/index.js`. The mismatch meant the lookup missed for essentially every SD that actually had a PRD, firing the false recommendation — recorded 3x as issue pattern `SAL-VALIDATION-REC` and auto-escalated into this SD via `/learn`. Fix: query by `sd_id` (the UUID-bearing column), matching the pattern already used correctly by `HandoffOrchestrator.js` and `PlanToExecVerifier.js`. `checkExistingPRD` is now exported with an injectable `client` param (defaults to the module-level client) for unit testability, with zero behavior change for its sole caller.
  - **Verification**: `tests/unit/sub-agents/validation-check-existing-prd.test.js` (3 new tests, including an explicit regression guard proving the pre-fix column would have missed); full `tests/unit/sub-agents/` suite (139 tests, 12 files) green, no regressions. Dogfooded live: re-ran the fixed VALIDATION sub-agent against its own SD and against SD-LEO-INFRA-LLM-FACTORY-TIER-LADDER-001 (a real completed SD with a PRD) — both correctly report "PRD exists" now. Backend-only, no schema/dependency changes. TESTING / VALIDATION / REGRESSION sub-agents all PASS (95-100% confidence); gates L2P 96 / P2E 95 / E2P 93 / P2L 94 / LEAD-FINAL 98.
- **Layer 4.3 "Migration File Validation" CI job no longer false-flags every PR/push on a months-old, already-merged migration** - PR #5433, #5436 (SD-LEO-FIX-DIFF-SCOPE-LAYER-001)
  - **What shipped**: `.github/workflows/retrospective-quality-gates.yml`'s `migration-validation` job ran `find database/migrations -name "*retrospective*.sql"` repo-wide and diff-independent, so it re-checked every retrospective migration on every run regardless of what the PR/push actually touched — false-flagging on `database/migrations/20260528_retrospective_type_default_null.sql` (merged via PR #4044, missing `BEGIN;`/`COMMIT;`) and failing every subsequent PR/push through this job. Adds `scripts/lint/compute-changed-retro-migrations.mjs` (pure `resolveDiffBase`/`computeFilesToCheck` decision functions) diff-scoping the job to only the retrospective migration files actually changed in the current diff — mirroring the existing `schema-reference-lint.yml` pattern for `pull_request`, and designing the `push`-trigger case net-new since no repo precedent existed for it. Fail-safe: an unresolvable diff base (fetch failure, or a `push` event's all-zeros `before` SHA on a new branch/force-push) falls back to the original full repo-wide sweep rather than silently skipping validation, since this is a hard-blocking correctness gate, not an advisory lint. The BEGIN/COMMIT/verification/rollback grep checks themselves are unchanged.
  - **Verification**: 15/15 unit tests pass (97.43% statement coverage) covering both the pure diff-scoping decisions and the `execSync`-mocked git/find wiring. Live-reproduced the false-flag (`20260528_retrospective_type_default_null.sql` genuinely lacks `BEGIN;`/`COMMIT;`) and confirmed the fix grandfathers it. Live-verified all 3 real event paths (`pull_request` vs `origin/main`, `push` with a real `before` SHA, `push` with the all-zeros sentinel). The exact "Layer 4.3" CI job passed on this change's own PR. Backend-only, no schema/dependency changes.
- **Chairman decision watcher no longer crashes on a Realtime channel error** - PR #5305 (SD-FDBK-ENH-CANARY-VENTURE-PROBE-001)
  - **What shipped**: `waitForDecision()` (`lib/eva/chairman-decision-watcher.js`) fell straight to its polling fallback on Realtime `CHANNEL_ERROR`/`TIMED_OUT` without ever tearing down the errored channel via `supabase.removeChannel()`. The still-subscribed-but-errored channel triggered the vendored `@supabase/realtime-js` phoenix client's `Channel.trigger`/`onClose` to recurse infinitely, crashing the process with `RangeError: Maximum call stack size exceeded` — reproduced twice in the Canary Venture Probe CI workflow. The fix removes the channel and nulls the reference before polling begins.
  - **Verification**: 16/16 tests pass in `tests/unit/eva/chairman-decision-watcher.test.js`, including 2 new fake-timer regression tests; independently confirmed by the TESTING sub-agent (PASS, 92% confidence). Backend-only, no schema/dependency changes. A post-merge re-run of the Canary Venture Probe workflow is the remaining real-world confirmation step.
- **EVA stage-governance and reality-gates no longer crash on a Realtime channel error — the sibling defect the previous fix left open** - PR #5308 (SD-FDBK-FIX-EVA-STAGE-GOVERNANCE-001)
  - **What shipped**: A post-merge re-run of the Canary Venture Probe workflow (done specifically to verify the SD-FDBK-ENH-CANARY-VENTURE-PROBE-001 fix above) reproduced the *identical* `RangeError: Maximum call stack size exceeded` crash from two different, un-migrated call sites: `lib/eva/stage-governance.js` and `lib/eva/reality-gates.js` both called a Realtime channel's own `unsubscribe()` re-entrantly from inside that channel's `.subscribe()` status callback on `CHANNEL_ERROR`/`CLOSED`/`TIMED_OUT`, letting the vendored phoenix client's `Channel.trigger`/`onClose` recurse infinitely. The fix extracts the already-proven pattern into a shared `lib/eva/realtime-channel-utils.js` helper (`safeRemoveChannel()` — null the reference, then `supabase.removeChannel()`) and applies it to both confirmed sites. Two other RCA-flagged candidates (`s20-pause-controller.js`, `venture-monitor.js`) were independently read and confirmed to already tear down channels correctly — left untouched.
  - **Verification**: 6 new regression tests (3 per file) construct a mock channel whose `unsubscribe()` recursively re-invokes its own status callback, proving `removeChannel()` breaks the chain; 185/185 dependent-module tests pass (18 files, 0 regressions). Independently confirmed by the TESTING (PASS, 95%) and REGRESSION (PASS, 95% — public API of both modules confirmed byte-identical apart from the internal teardown fix) sub-agents. Backend-only, no schema/dependency changes. A post-merge re-run of the Canary Venture Probe workflow is the remaining real-world confirmation step.

## 2026-06-20

### Infrastructure
- **The sourcing engine gains its chairman decision-queue lane — candidates that need an authority only the chairman can grant (or that wait on an operational outcome) now have a durable, SLA'd, idempotent home instead of evaporating as a transient prose ask** - PR #4899 (SD-LEO-INFRA-SOURCING-ENGINE-CHAIRMAN-QUEUE-001)
  - **What shipped**: Sourcing engine child 4/10. The router (child 1) lanes some intake candidates to `chairman-gated` (needs a grant/rls/credential/operational/vision authority) or `outcome-gated` (buildable only after a venture earns an operational outcome), but there was nowhere durable for them to land. This adds **`sourcing_chairman_queue`** via an **additive, idempotent migration** (`CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` with a `state` CHECK enum `pending|decided|deferred_until|escalated`, a `UNIQUE (source_id, gate_type)` idempotency key, a `context` jsonb carrying the routed payload, SLA columns, and two indexes), plus **`lib/sourcing-engine/escalator.js`** — a pure `buildQueueRow` (chairman-gated → 72h SLA + the authority; outcome-gated → 168h SLA + enablers; null for non-queue lanes) and a fail-soft `escalateToChairmanQueue` that idempotently upserts one row per `(source_id, gate_type)`, **refuses a null/empty `source_id`** (in Postgres `NULL != NULL`, so a null key would silently re-insert and flood the queue), and **never throws** — a missing client, the DORMANT table, or a thrown transport error each return a structured `degraded` verdict. Ships **DORMANT**: the fleet authors and tests the migration; Adam applies this additive `CREATE TABLE` via the database-agent under the chairman's additive-DDL delegation (not chairman-gated — fleet-internal queue state, no RLS), and the escalator degrades until it is live.
  - **Verification**: 18 hermetic unit tests (per-lane row building, the idempotent/fail-soft/null-source upsert paths, a real `routeCandidate` integration, and migration-file content) plus 1 DORMANT `*.db.test.js` live probe that **skips until the migration is applied** (never a false failure). `npx vitest run tests/unit/sourcing-engine/` → **26 passed / 3 skipped** (the dormant probes). Independent adversarial review returned **SHIP** and caught the null-`source_id` idempotency hole (fixed pre-ship with a `no_source_id` guard + a 3-case covering test asserting zero DB writes); lane strings were live-confirmed to match the router↔lane vocabulary exactly. TESTING / VALIDATION / REGRESSION all PASS (conf 96); Heal 93/100; gates P2E 97 / E2P 94 / P2L 95 / LEAD-FINAL 98.

## 2026-06-19

### Infrastructure
- **The 'EHG % built' vision gauge now measures the FOUNDATION honestly — 4 revenue/operating capabilities that can only progress once a venture earns moved from the active V1 rung to the future V2 rung, so V1% rises by building instead of being capped by income it can't yet realize** - PR #4891 (SD-LEO-INFRA-VISION-LADDER-V1-V2-RECUT-001)
  - **What shipped**: Chairman-ratified vision re-cut. Four V1 capabilities (*Take a real dollar*, *See distance-to-quit*, *Run a self-operating venture*, *Compound venture-level learning*) are revenue/operating outcomes that **cannot progress without a venture earning** — leaving them in the active V1 rung made V1% conflate *foundation built* with *income realized* (it could never approach 100% by building). This re-points those 4 `vision_ladder_criteria` rows from the active **V1** rung to the inactive **V2** rung (V1 25→21, V2 1→5) and, in **lockstep**, removes their 4 probes from the active `VDR_REGISTRY` (25→21) and `OPERATIONAL_NATURE` (10→6) so `assertRegistryCoherence` byte-matches the new 21-criterion active rung. **No V2 probe is added** — a probe for an inactive rung is a staleProbe that withholds the whole gauge (anti-honesty-lie); the 4 return only when V2 activates. Net effect: **V1% = is the foundation built** (rose **43% → 60%**, with `build_pct` **88%** as the 4 operational zeros leave the V1 denominator), and **V2% = are we earning** (0% until a venture operates). `assertLadderRoadmapCoherence` (the enforce-side) is a separate sibling SD and out of scope here.
  - **Verification**: The DB↔code lockstep is **atomic** — coherence is an exact string-set match between the live active-rung criteria and `VDR_REGISTRY`; any mismatch makes the gauge honestly *withhold* (never a wrong number), so the DB move was applied and the code merged in tight succession (window minimized) and confirmed reconciled. Live: `coherence.ok=true`, `available=true`, `total_capabilities=21`, `build_pct=88`, `overall_pct=60`. 96/96 vision tests green (taxonomy recut to 21/6, stub gauge math recomputed 11→7 / 18→7, an FR-5 regression that the 4 are not probed while V2 inactive) plus 2 non-vision sibling count pins fixed in PR #4894 (the REGRESSION sub-agent caught them). TESTING / VALIDATION (conf 98) / REGRESSION all PASS; Heal 95/100; gates P2L 98 / LEAD-FINAL 99.
- **The sourcing engine gets its schema foundation — a mutable `lane` routing column (separate from the terminal disposition) plus one canonical lane vocabulary every engine component shares** - PR #4886 (SD-LEO-INFRA-SOURCING-ENGINE-LEDGER-LANE-COLUMN-001)
  - **What shipped**: Sourcing engine child 2/10. The router (child 1) computes a routing **lane** for each intake item, but there was nowhere to persist it — `conversion_ledger` and `roadmap_wave_items` carried only a terminal `disposition`. This adds a **separate, mutable `lane text` column** (nullable) to both tables via an **additive, idempotent migration** (`ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` + an additive `CHECK` enumerating the 5 lanes `belt-ready|chairman-gated|outcome-gated|dedup|decline` plus the parametric `blocked-on-<blocker>`, NULL allowed), and introduces **`lib/sourcing-engine/lane.js`** — one canonical lane vocabulary (`LANE`/`FIXED_LANES`/`blockedLane`/`isValidLane`) kept in **lockstep with the DB CHECK** that the router and every downstream writer (register-first stamping, dedup-autostamp, populator) import rather than each duplicating the set. `lane` is deliberately kept distinct from `disposition` — two axes, never overloaded. Ships **DORMANT**: the fleet authors and tests the migration; Adam applies this additive nullable-column migration via the database-agent under the chairman's additive-DDL delegation (not chairman-gated — no RLS needed), and the engine fail-softs (degrades) until it is live.

- **Every operational loop can now declare HOW its goal is judged (deterministic vs LLM-as-judge) and WHAT it costs to run — and a judge-style loop without a defined rubric is rejected at validation** - PR #4881 (SD-LEO-INFRA-LOOP-CONTRACT-GOAL-TYPE-BUDGET-001)
  - **What shipped**: Extends the canonical loop-contract framework (`lib/loops/`) on the two distinctions the autonomous-loop model turns on. **(1) Goal type** — a frozen `GOAL_TYPE {verifiable, llm_as_judge}` enum; goals evolve from bare strings to typed `{description, type, metric?, rubric_ref?}`. A `llm_as_judge` goal **MUST** carry a `rubric_ref` — the **fail-loud anti-brittleness guard**, because a judge-evaluated loop without a defined rubric is exactly the brittle failure mode to block; a `verifiable` goal *should* carry a deterministic `metric`. Bare-string goals stay valid (back-compat), and the validator remains pure and total. **(2) Run-budget** — an optional `budget {tokens_per_run_estimate?, daily_max_runs?, pause_if_budget_below_pct?}` so the registry can scale past its 2 exemplars to many hourly loops without collective budget exhaustion (declaration only — enforcement/auto-pause in the cron executor is a documented follow-on). Both registry exemplars are migrated to typed goals + budgets; the Adam opportunity-scan's rationale-bar goal is now declared `llm_as_judge` pointing at the real `lib/adam/rationale-bar.js`. Declaring a loop still changes nothing about how it runs.
  - **Verification**: 21 new tests (44 total in `tests/unit/loops/`); the judge-rubric guard was **mutation-tested** by an independent adversarial reviewer (neutralizing it fails exactly one test — it is a real guard, not a tautology), verdict **SHIP** (0 HIGH/MEDIUM). Back-compat confirmed: the 23 base tests still pass, bare-string goals still validate, and there are zero importers of the module outside `lib/loops/`. Additive, single-repo, no schema change, no runtime behavior change. TESTING / VALIDATION (conf 96) / REGRESSION (conf 96) all PASS; Heal 96/100; gates P2L 100 / LEAD-FINAL approved.
- **/distill stops silently stranding chairman-reviewed videos in the YouTube For-Processing playlist — the archive step actually runs again, and any future breakage is now loud instead of swallowed** - PR #4876 (SD-LEO-INFRA-DISTILL-ARCHIVE-PATH-AND-YT-PROCESSED-001)
  - **What shipped**: Three compounding bugs had quietly broken the /distill Step-5 archive (move reviewed items to the Processed playlist / complete Todoist tasks). (1) The pipeline invoked `node scripts/eva-intake-archive.js`, but that file had been relocated to `scripts/archive/one-time/` (ENOENT) — it now logged a soft "Archive had errors" and continued. (2) The relocated script's `../lib/integrations/post-processor.js` import no longer resolved from its new folder. (3) `lib/integrations/post-processor.js` `postProcessYouTube` had no `status='processed'` selection branch (unlike `postProcessTodoist`), so once the review/cluster step marked a video `processed`, the YouTube move could **never** pick it up — videos were "processed" in the DB but stayed in For-Processing indefinitely. The fix **restores the script to `scripts/`** via `git mv` (one move repairs both the pipeline path *and* the `../lib` import, since that relative import is only correct from `scripts/`), **adds the missing `reviewedItems` (`status='processed'` + `processed_at` NULL) and orphan-recovery (`pending` + `chairman_reviewed_at`) branches** to `postProcessYouTube` mirroring the Todoist side, with a **`dedupeById` guard** for the classified∩orphan double-insert hazard (YouTube playlist inserts are not idempotent), and makes any future archive failure **loud + durable**: a `::error::` annotation plus an idempotent `feedback` row via `log-harness-bug.js`, with the archive script now exiting non-zero on per-item errors so partial failures reach the pipeline.
  - **Verification**: `tests/unit/distill-archive-yt-processed.test.js` — 8 tests incl. a functional `postProcessYouTube` run (recording Supabase + mocked YouTube client) that **fails if the fix is reverted** (mutation-tested); 71/71 green across the intake + post-processor folders (no regression in the deduped Todoist sibling). Independent adversarial review verdict **SHIP** (0 HIGH/MEDIUM): confirmed the rename is clean with zero dangling references, the new branches mirror the Todoist union exactly, the double-insert hazard is defended, and the fail-loud wiring is runtime-verified end-to-end. TESTING / VALIDATION (conf 94) / REGRESSION (conf 97) all PASS; Heal 96/100; gates P2L 100 / LEAD-FINAL approved. (Adam had manually corrected 25 stranded videos beforehand; this fixes the root cause. Live YouTube move not re-exercised — 0 stranded rows remain and the API daily quota was exhausted — so verification is code-level + the unit/mutation tests.)
- **The automated 'EHG % built' gauge can finally see the EHG app repo — its 3 EHG-targeted capability probes stop being perpetually 'unknown' so the vision % covers all 25 capabilities, not 22/25** - PR #4869 (SD-LEO-INFRA-VISION-GAUGE-CRON-EHG-CHECKOUT-001)
  - **What shipped**: The hourly Adam exec-email cron (`.github/workflows/adam-exec-email-cron.yml`) runs the VDR vision gauge, but it only ever checked out `EHG_Engineer`. Three of the 25 `VDR_REGISTRY` capabilities (distance-to-broke, venture-performance read, the operator cockpit) are `code_grep` probes that target the **separate, private `rickfelix/ehg` app repo** — which was never on the runner, so the grep seam honestly banded them `'unknown'` and the automated vision % was computed over only 22/25 (and could never reflect EHG-app completions). This adds a **2nd `actions/checkout`** for `rickfelix/ehg` (fail-soft `continue-on-error`, `persist-credentials: false`), **reusing the established `GH_TOKEN_CROSS_REPO` org secret** already used by the other two cross-repo workflows (with a repo-local `EHG_RO_PAT` documented as the fallback), and exports **`VDR_EHG_REPO_ROOT`** — the grep seam's own env override (`lib/vision/vdr-grep-seam.js resolveRepoRoots`) — at the checkout path so the 3 probes resolve. A **loud, outcome-gated, non-blocking `::warning title=VDR gauge coverage <25/25::`** annotation surfaces (in every cron run) exactly why coverage is <25/25 whenever the checkout is unavailable, so the gap is never silent. Fully merge-safe: if the cross-repo token is absent the checkout 404s, the cron + chairman email continue uninterrupted, and the gauge degrades to 22/25 *exactly as today* (the seam never fabricates `'built'`); the next hourly snapshot auto-upgrades to 25/25 once a token is present — no further code change.
  - **Verification**: Live read-only gauge replay — with `VDR_EHG_REPO_ROOT` pointed at an `ehg` checkout, `computeBuildGauge` yields **denominator = 25, unknown_count = 0** (the 3 ehg probes band partial/unbuilt, never 'built'); without it, **22/3** (the pre-fix state). An independent adversarial review upgraded the change from "dormant-until-an-operator-provisions-a-new-secret" to **works-on-merge** by switching to the already-provisioned `GH_TOKEN_CROSS_REPO`, and caught a source-pin test that anchored on a YAML *comment* mention of the repo rather than the real `repository:` config (tightened). A first wrong-knob attempt (an `EHG_REPO_PATH` override on `lib/repo-paths.js`) was caught by live testing — the gauge's seam reads `VDR_EHG_REPO_ROOT`, not repo-paths — and reverted git-clean. 22/22 unit tests green (5 new YAML source-pin + 17 grep-seam); REGRESSION confirmed the diff is purely additive (0 deletions, existing cron steps byte-unchanged). Heal 96/100 (PASS); VALIDATION + REGRESSION sub-agents both PASS; gates P2L 99 / LEAD-FINAL 99.
- **'EHG % built' stops conflating fleet build-debt with future-staged venture operation — the chairman now sees an honest fleet-build % alongside the all-criteria rung %** - PR #4863 (SD-LEO-INFRA-GAUGE-BUILDABLE-VS-OPERATIONAL-001)
  - **What shipped**: The VDR gauge's headline number lumped together two very different things: a *buildable* capability the fleet simply hasn't shipped yet (real build-debt) and an *operational* proof that is correctly 0 until a real venture runs (e.g. "take a real dollar", "run a self-operating venture"). This segregates them **without changing the honest all-criteria number**. Each of the 25 `VDR_REGISTRY` capabilities gets a deterministic `nature` ('buildable' | 'operational') via a single reviewable `OPERATIONAL_NATURE` set (the 10 KR/chairman/venture/competitive-signal proofs) guarded by a module-load fail-loud drift assertion; `computeBuildGauge` now exposes a **`build_pct`** over buildable capabilities only and an **`operational_pct`**/status over the operational set, **alongside the byte-unchanged `overall_pct`** (anti-honesty-lie doctrine preserved — unknowns still excluded from all three, operational still shown honestly, never folded into the build %). The Adam exec-summary now **leads with the fleet-build %** as the honest 'built' number, shows V1 rung-completion separately, and labels operational rungs *"awaiting venture operation (V2 precursor)"* instead of silently counting them as 0% built (no emojis; the Chairman-UI tile's `pct` stays back-compatible). The capability-gap sourcing lens excludes operational capabilities so Adam never ranks an un-sourceable operational proof as a build target.
  - **Verification**: Live read-only gauge replay — `overall_pct` **43%** (UNCHANGED, all-criteria) vs `build_pct` **88%** (the fleet has built most of what it *can* build) vs `operational_pct` **25%** (10 proofs: 2 flipped, 8 awaiting venture operation), all re-derived from components and matched. 9 hermetic unit tests (taxonomy completeness, segregated compute re-derived from components, exec-summary rendering, gauge-lens exclusion); 309 tests green across the vision + adam folders. An independent adversarial review verdict was **SHIP** (0 HIGH/MEDIUM) — confirmed the `overall_pct` math byte-unchanged, unknowns excluded from all three, the 15-buildable/10-operational classification defensible per borderline capability, the fail-loud assertion correct, and the sourcing-lens exclusion correct; one LOW cosmetic was fixed. - **The coordinator sweep no longer false-BLOCKs work whose dependencies are already done — claimable SDs stop being hidden behind phantom "deps unmet" lines** - PR #4856 (SD-LEO-INFRA-SWEEP-DEP-RESOLVER-COMPLETED-LOOKUP-001)
  - **What shipped**: A one-class fix to `scripts/stale-session-sweep.cjs`. The sweep built its dependency *satisfied-set* (`completedKeys`) from the in-memory standalone working set — which is queried with `.in('status',['draft','in_progress','ready','pending_approval']).limit(20)` and therefore **can never contain a completed SD** — so `completedKeys` was effectively empty and **any** SD with a real completed dependency-key was printed `BLOCKED (deps unmet)` every tick. The fix mirrors the canonical resolver in `scripts/coordinator-audit.mjs`: a **fresh batched `.in('sd_key', allDepKeys)` lookup** of the exact dependency keys, checked against `SWEEP_DEP_TERMINAL = ['completed','cancelled','archived','deferred']` via `isDepSatisfied` (unknown/missing dep still counts unmet). The `available` and `blocked` filters now share that predicate; one batched query, guarded by `allDepKeys.length` (no N+1). It is the direct analog of the already-shipped SD-LEO-INFRA-DEP-RESOLVER-IGNORE-NON-SDKEY-001, which converged `coordinator-audit` onto the shared parser.
  - **Verification**: A **read-only live replay** (old in-memory set vs new fresh lookup) on the live working set caught a real case — the old logic falsely BLOCKED `SD-EHG-OPERATOR-CASH-BANK-FEED-001` because its dependency `SD-EHG-OPERATOR-RUNWAY-SUBSTRATE-001` was *completed but out-of-window*; the new logic correctly resolves it satisfied (**0 blocked**). 10 network-free unit tests (behavioral predicate: terminal satisfied / non-terminal+unknown blocked / mixed deps / prose dropped; plus source-pins for the fresh lookup + terminal set, and that the old in-memory build is gone). An independent adversarial review verdict was **SOUND (0 HIGH/MEDIUM)**. Heal 100/100; gates L2P / P2E / E2P / P2L / LEAD-FINAL 98. Follow-up flagged: converge the remaining independent fleet dep-resolvers (`fleet-dashboard`/`fleet-coaching`/`context-builder`) on one shared helper (PAT-COORDINATOR-DEP-EVAL-DIVERGENCE).
- **The chronically-red Unit Tier source-pin tests are green again — `npm run test:unit` passes on main, restoring the green-CI gate these pins exist to provide** - PR #4841 (SD-LEO-INFRA-UNIT-TIER-SOURCEPIN-REBASELINE-001)
  - **What shipped**: A triage-first re-baseline of the 14 live-failing Unit Tier source-pin test files (15 at LEAD; sibling SDs closed one before EXEC). The single genuine regression: `scripts/stale-session-sweep.cjs`'s fixture-session SD-release `UPDATE` nulled `claiming_session_id` without co-clearing `active_session_id` (the FR-1 claim-lifecycle invariant; the omitting site was introduced by PR #4691, and the sync trigger's CAS branch can't cover a value pointing at another session) — **fixed at source** (added `active_session_id: null` to match the other 4 release sites) and both guard tests were *strengthened* to pin the invariant, not relaxed. - **The fleet's source-to-capacity + decompose-weakest-layer sourcing rules are now canonical in the coordinator and Adam role contracts — not just session memory** - PR #4832 (SD-LEO-INFRA-SOURCING-CAPACITY-CANONICALIZE-001)
  - **What shipped**: Two chairman-directed fleet-sourcing rules were written into the DB-backed LEO role contracts (`leo_protocol_sections`, the source that `scripts/generate-claude-md-from-db.js` renders into `CLAUDE_COORDINATOR.md` + `CLAUDE_ADAM.md`), so both roles follow them durably instead of from drifting feedback-backlog notes. **SOURCE-TO-CAPACITY** (coordinator, id=605): the belt-low ping to Adam now MUST include the **live idle-worker count** (resolved from the roll-call / `claude_sessions`), Adam sizes the shortlist to ~that many conflict-free candidates, and the coordinator ranks the returned shortlist by **gauge-weakness** and **dispatches one capability per idle worker**. **DECOMPOSE-WEAKEST-LAYER** (Adam, id=604): when the VDR build-% gauge's weakest *layer* holds N weak capabilities (e.g. the application/cockpit layer), Adam sources up to **N parallel** one-per-capability conflict-free design/spec SDs — sized to idle capacity — instead of one monolithic SD per belt-low cycle. The two halves form a `min(N weak capabilities, idle capacity)` handshake that keeps the fleet parallelized across the whole weak layer.

- **The estate backlog (Todoist + YouTube + Claude-Code intake, 561 items) is now dispositioned into the conversion ledger with an auditable trace-back — without starving the enrichment pipelines** - PR #4815 (SD-LEO-INFRA-ESTATE-DISPOSITION-001)

The **mark-off writes ONLY `raw_data`** (the ledger back-pointer is the authoritative idempotency marker) and deliberately never touches the source `status`/`processed_at` columns — those gate each table's enrichment pipeline (release-analyzer / youtube post-processor / todoist), so a re-run or the new hourly cron never re-disposes a row and never starves a pipeline. ### Features
- **An honest operator cash/burn substrate so the cockpit's distance-to-broke gauge can be measured, not guessed** - PR #4850 (SD-EHG-OPERATOR-RUNWAY-SUBSTRATE-001)
  - **What shipped**: An operator-grain monthly cash/burn substrate (`operator_cash_burn_monthly`, additive, applied live) whose single contract is **never fabricate a financial number**. Every input — cash, AI burn, other burn, revenue — carries its own `last_synced_at`; a missing input is **NULL (unattested), never 0**, and a stale input is **suppressed** to *"stale / not yet measurable"* rather than shown as live (mirroring the `replacement-net-source` NULL-not-zero precedent + the `cloud-cap-feeder` liveness-window precedent). A **fail-soft hourly feed** (`scripts/operator/feed-operator-cash-burn.mjs` + a new cron) totals the last 30 days of measured AI spend (via `scripts/llm-cost-report.mjs`) and writes it to the substrate **and** the live `income_capture_monthly.business_expenses` slot, **always labeled a lower bound** (main-session Opus tokens are structurally uncaptured); it mirrors the existing auto-derived `recurring_revenue` as the inflow partial with its **test-mode** flag surfaced honestly; and it backfills `venture_token_ledger.cost_usd` for **resolvable models only**. A `getDistanceToBroke()` accessor renders **months-of-runway only when cash AND net-burn are both fresh** — otherwise it returns the honest partials it has plus an *"awaiting cash source"* headline. This is the data contract the cockpit's distance-to-broke tile (separate, dependency-blocked SD) reads.
  - **Verification**: Live-verified — AI burn **$142.01** (lower bound) + revenue **$25** (test-mode) written; cash absent ⇒ runway **withheld** as *"awaiting cash source"*; net-burn **$117.01**; no fabricated number. 14 unit tests for the honest-degrade logic (freshness windows, stale-suppression, NULL-not-zero, net-positive withholding); 100 tests green across touched modules. An independent adversarial review verdict was **SOUND (0 HIGH)** and caught one MEDIUM — the AI-burn `business_expenses` write was livemode-agnostic (a meaningless test-row write that would silently feed the distance-to-quit glide-path once a live row exists) — **fixed** by scoping it to the live operator row with the intentional coupling documented. Honest follow-up: `venture_token_ledger.model_id` is unpopulated, so per-venture AI cost prices $0 today (a data-capture gap, not a fabrication). Heal 100/100; gates L2P 95 / P2E 72 (stories rewritten 28%→72%) / E2P / P2L 80 / LEAD-FINAL 96 (26/26 gates).

- **Shared-root resync no longer wipes gitignored runtime state — a canonical safe-resync helper replaces ad-hoc `git clean -fdx`** - PR #4768 (SD-LEO-INFRA-SHARED-ROOT-RESYNC-SAFETY-001)
  - **What shipped**: `scripts/safe-root-resync.mjs` (`npm run resync:safe`) — the canonical shared-root SYNC step, wired into `docs/protocol/fleet-coordinator-and-worker-behavior.md`. Default path is non-destructive (`git fetch` + `git merge --ff-only origin/main`, dirty-tree skip, and a hard worktree-guard abort when `.git` is a file). Untracked cleanup is DOUBLE-gated: `--clean-untracked` only prints the `git clean -fdn` dry-run preview, and the actual `git clean -fd` requires a second explicit `--confirm-clean`. No code path can construct `-x`, so gitignored runtime state (`node_modules/`, `.claude/active-coordinator.json`) is always preserved — closing the 3 confirmed prod incidents. A fail-open `restoreAfterResync()` tail re-registers the coordinator pointer (reusing the shipped `restoreCoordinatorPointer` hook) and repairs a broken `node_modules` via a bounded `npm install` that runs ONLY when this session owns the cross-session mutex, with a timeout bounded strictly below `LOCK_TTL_MS` so a slow install can never outlive the lock and overlap a second session's install.
  - **Verification**: `tests/unit/scripts/safe-root-resync.test.js` 15/15 (no-x invariant, worktree guard, double-confirm clean gate, lock-ownership bail, install-timeout < lock-TTL invariant, fail-open tail). Three adversarial-review rounds converged (5 findings → 1 HIGH → 0 new). `docs/runbooks/safe-root-resync.md` documents operation, exit codes, and the data-safety contract. Heal 93/100; gates E2P 95 / P2L 96.

- **Adam's role contract now TEACHES the SD-creation how-to + its duties (not just names them)** - PR #4773 (SD-LEO-INFRA-ADAM-ROLE-CONTRACT-001)
  - **What shipped**: A new `leo_protocol_sections` row (`section_type=adam_role_contract`, id=604) authored in the DB and rendered into `CLAUDE_ADAM.md` via `scripts/generate-claude-md-from-db.js` (never hand-edited). It teaches the SD-creation HOW-TO — the required NOT-NULL fields; the VERIFIED JSONB shapes (`success_criteria={criterion,measure}`, `key_changes={change,impact}` — NOT `{change,type}`); the canonical `/sd-create` create path + the `ENF-SD-CREATE-SKILL` block; and the keyword type-inference hazard (standalone `fix` matches before `infrastructure`) + the `docs→docs` `mapToDbType` caveat — plus procedural teaching of the conversion, build-% gauge (Vision Denominator Registry), and escalation duties, referencing `CLAUDE_LEAD.md` rather than duplicating it. Child C of SD-LEO-INFRA-ADAM-AUTONOMY-HARDENING-001 (closes the chairman keystone 2026-06-13: a LEO role is reliable because its required-reading contract CONTAINS the how-to).
  - **Verification**: a 3-lens adversarial content review (accuracy-vs-code / does-it-teach / no-drift) caught 4 real accuracy errors, all corrected verbatim-from-code; drift guard green (`check-claude-md-drift.cjs`); TESTING PASS 95 / VALIDATION PASS 100. Gates L2P 94 / P2E 99 / E2P 96 / P2L 100 / LEAD-FINAL 99; heal 92/100.

### Infrastructure
- **Adam advisories now survive long enough for the coordinator to read them — every advisory gets a durable 24h delivery TTL instead of expiring before the ~15min coordinator inbox poll** - PR #4746 (SD-LEO-INFRA-ADAM-ADVISORY-COMMS-001)
  - **What shipped**: `scripts/adam-advisory.cjs` — a pure, exported `advisoryExpiresAt(nowMs)` helper now stamps a mode-INDEPENDENT 24h `expires_at` on every advisory row, replacing the request-mode `timeoutMs + 5min` branch whose ~6min window let an advisory be swept by the expired-row sweep before the coordinator’s ~15min inbox poll ever saw it (RCA 076cf785, the 5th Adam→coordinator comms-loss mode). `timeoutMs` is now decoupled and bounds ONLY the synchronous `awaitCoordinatorReply` window, not row durability. FR1 of the ADAM-MACHINERY-CONSUMER parent.
  - **Verification**: `tests/unit/adam-advisory-comms.test.js` 8/8. The TTL-vs-await decoupling is self-documented in-code at the `advisoryExpiresAt` definition and the `expiresAt` fix site (both cite the SD key + RCA 076cf785).

- **A session reconnect no longer silently demotes a coordinator or drops its claim — `create_or_replace_session` now merges session metadata instead of overwriting it** - PR #4742 (SD-LEO-INFRA-FIX-CREATE-REPLACE-001)
  - **What shipped**: The `create_or_replace_session` RPC's `ON CONFLICT (session_id)` branch set `metadata = EXCLUDED.metadata`, replacing the entire `claude_sessions.metadata` JSONB on every session re-init — silently wiping `is_coordinator` and claim flags the live session already carried (a routine reconnect could demote a coordinator or drop claim state). Changed to a shallow merge: `metadata = COALESCE(claude_sessions.metadata,'{}'::jsonb) || COALESCE(EXCLUDED.metadata,'{}'::jsonb)`, so keys the re-init caller omits are preserved while keys it re-passes still win. Rebased on the **current** live definition (`20260509`: `sd_key` + `claiming_session_id`), not the stale `20260201` body (which referenced a since-removed `sd_id` column). The same replace bug in `lib/session-manager.mjs`'s two RPC-failure fallback `upsert()` paths was fixed in parallel (merge against the existing row first). Migration is additive / idempotent (`CREATE OR REPLACE`) / reversible; prod apply is chairman-gated.
  - **Verification**: An in-migration `DO $verify$` ASSERT block self-verifies the merge at apply time, plus a `tests/db-invariants` test that applies the corrected function inside a **rolled-back transaction** (proving real behavior against the live schema with zero permanent change) and a static regression guard — 2/2 green. Adversarial review surfaced 4 findings, all addressed (incl. the in-scope fallback-upsert sibling bug). Gates L2P 94 / P2E 95 / E2P 97 / P2L 97 / LEAD-FINAL 99.

- **Fleet workers and the coordinator now get an advisory warning when their local checkout is stale — and a hard STALE-CRITICAL flag when a CLAUDE*.md protocol file has drifted, so no one silently operates on out-of-date rules** - PR #4733 (SD-LEO-INFRA-FLEET-FRESHNESS-GUARD-001)
  - **What shipped**: `lib/governance/checkout-freshness.js` — ONE reusable, FAIL-OPEN guard generalizing the scattered behind-count + path-scoped-diff patterns. A PURE verdict fn (`evaluateFreshness`) + an injectable-IO sync reader (`checkoutFreshness`, git seam via `execFileSync` — no shell, cross-platform) + a `freshnessBadge` one-liner + frozen `CRITICAL_PROTOCOL_FILES`. Verdict precedence STALE-CRITICAL > STALE > FRESH; STALE-CRITICAL fires on a CLAUDE*.md drift detected via a **two-dot** `git diff HEAD..base` (three-dot would diff the merge-base and false-FRESH a local hand-edit at behind=0 — the exact drift the guard exists to catch). EVERY git error fail-opens to FRESH so a freshness check can NEVER block startup or an audit; `fetch` is opt-in (default off) for fast/offline-safe startup. Wired advisory + non-blocking into `scripts/adam-startup-check.mjs`, `scripts/coordinator-startup-check.mjs` (badge in `buildReport`), and `scripts/coordinator-charter-audit.mjs` (advisory dimension kept OUT of the violation count).
  - **Verification**: 20/20 tests (15 unit incl. precedence/coercion/fail-open + 5 real-git integration). Canonical API doc is the in-module JSDoc contract header.

- **Durable read-only coordinator charter-compliance self-audit with named remediations** - PR #4729 (SD-LEO-INFRA-COORDINATOR-CHARTER-SELF-AUDIT-001)
  - **What shipped**: `scripts/coordinator-charter-audit.mjs` (`npm run coordinator:charter-audit`) + pure detectors in `lib/coordinator/charter-audit-detectors.mjs`, wired into `STANDARD_LOOPS` (`coordinator-startup-check.mjs`) so it survives a coordinator session restart (replacing a lost session-only CronCreate). Hardens the inline SRE-gauges: **fail-loud** on foundational SD/session queries (a column error inline silently returned `[]` = false all-clean); **authoritative liveness** (heartbeat OR in-window armed-silence OR a live PID via the sweep `resolveCcPidFromTerminalId`) so a long-EXEC/armed-silence worker is not miscounted idle/dead; + 3 new duty checks (worktrees N/20, backlog-rank staleness, QUIET-TICK committed-action).
  - **Verification**: 32 detector unit + 10 startup-check tests pass; live-smoke validated (read-only; real per-duty gauges + `CHARTER_AUDIT_VIOLATIONS=2`). A 9-agent adversarial review found + fixed 4 major defects, all in the audit's own false-clean/false-alive/false-positive classes: DUTY-1 fail-loud was unreachable (`countActiveWorktrees` swallows git errors → compare git vs filesystem); liveness ignored `status` (a RELEASED+fresh-heartbeat session read ALIVE → dispatch to a dead session); `extractDepKey` object branch bypassed the SD-key rule (`{sd_key:'none'}` → false ANOMALY); the unclaimed/claimable belt was looser than canonical (an orchestrator PARENT got recommended for dispatch → route through `classifyDispatchIneligibility`). VALIDATION PASS (fail-loud empirically proven), RETRO 90. Gates L2P 95 / P2E 93 / E2P 92 / P2L 96 / LEAD-FINAL 99.

- **Scripts estate reconciliation: weekly reachability gauge + scratch-sweep extension + liveness norm + first 102-file archive batch** - PRs #4626 (code) + #4629 (moves) (SD-LEO-INFRA-SCRIPTS-ESTATE-RECONCILIATION-001)

- **Archive-not-delete retention for 6 unbounded audit/trace tables — live, chairman-approved, 196k rows archived** - PRs #4566 + #4570 (SD-LEO-INFRA-RETENTION-POLICY-UNBOUNDED-001)
  - **Issue**: Six tables grew unbounded with no retention (workflow_trace_log 607k, governance_audit_log 605k, audit_log 143k, validation_audit_log 59k, model_usage_log 52k, permission_audit_log 41k rows), degrading hot governance queries and inflating backups.
  - **Fix**: One reversible migration (`retention_archive` cold JSONB store — restore = re-insert `row_data` — + `retention_runs` age-keyed liveness stamps: alarm on AGE of max(ran_at), never self-reported status); declarative policy registry with VERIFIED per-table timestamp columns, 90d windows (3x the 30d longest enforced consumer lookback found by the validation sweep) and a MIN_HOT_DAYS=45 floor that refuses to run below it; batched enforcement CLI (`npm run retention:check/apply`) with the archive-BEFORE-delete invariant (failed archive ⇒ zero deletes), per-table fail-soft, `--liveness`, `--arming-spec` (never self-arms), and daemon-log rotation. The mgmt-reviews quarantine table is tracked as a report-only soak entry (manual chairman drop after 2026-06-24).
  - **Live findings (both turned into non-events by the invariant design)**: (1) PostgREST silently caps SELECTs at max-rows=1000, so BATCH_SIZE=2000 truncated and the convergence check stopped after one batch — clamped to 1000 (#4570); (2) governance_audit_log statement timeouts on un-indexed changed_at sorts — archive-before-delete HELD on every timeout (zero unarchived deletes), counts converged across reruns; index follow-up flagged.
  - **Verification**: live BEGIN..ROLLBACK round-trip pre-apply; chairman GO with live dry-run evidence (~379k eligible); 196,007 rows archived (restorable JSONB verified); validation_audit_log/audit_log/model_usage_log fully converged to 0 rows >90d; 14/14 tests; TESTING PASS 96, VALIDATION PASS 92. Gates: 93/94/92/96, LEAD-FINAL 98; retro quality 100.
- **Class-level pattern escalation: site-diversity threshold auto-drafts propose-only class-fix SDs + the 5/5-FP corrective auto-finding path gated default-OFF** - PR #4579 (SD-LEO-INFRA-CLASS-LEVEL-PATTERN-001)
  - **Issue**: Recurring incident CLASSES escalated only when a human noticed — `issue_patterns.occurrence_count` counts repeats but cannot distinguish one site failing 5x (one fix) from 5 DIFFERENT sites failing identically (a structural class: artifact-type mismatches, phantom-column writes, exit-hangs all sat unescalated). The corrective-sd-generator built for auto-drafting produced 5/5 false positives (single-doc vision-tier complaints, zero site diversity).

Wired fail-soft into BOTH live recording seams (rca-orchestrator `upsertIssuePattern` update+insert — the PAT-AUTO writer — and issue-knowledge-base `recordOccurrence`), always AFTER the host write. `score-command.mjs`'s per-score auto-finding call gated default-OFF behind `CORRECTIVE_AUTO_FINDINGS` — NARROW (generator untouched; the weekly scheduler round + heal/triage flows unaffected, pinned by a static test). Dormant pattern-detection-engine (zero live callers) untouched.
  - **Verification**: historical backtest — the 3 known-good classes (artifact-type S21/22/23, phantom-column, exit-hang) each escalate at EXACTLY the 3rd distinct site; FP negatives (single-site 5x = the corrective-FP shape, noise, resolved, re-escalation) all hold. 19 new tests, 37/37 learning suites; TESTING PASS 96, VALIDATION PASS 92.
